[<p>\n<b>High:</b> 55\xb0 | <b>Low:</b> 53\xb0</p>, <p>\n<b>Chance of rain:</b>\r\n    \t\t    0%\r\n    \t\t    </p>, <p>\n<b>Wind:</b> WNW at 6mph</p>, <p class="p">\xa9 2018\xa0<a href="http://www.coxmediagroup.com" shape="rect" target="_blank">Cox Media Group</a></p>, <p class="p">The first meteor shower of 2019, the\xa0<a href="https://solarsystem.nasa.gov/asteroids-comets-and-meteors/meteors-and-meteorites/quadrantids/in-depth/" shape="rect" target="_blank">Quadrantid shower</a>, will light up the sky between Thursday, Jan. 3 and Friday, Jan. 4.</p>, <p dir="ltr" lang="en">Don't miss the <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/Quadrantid?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">#Quadrantid</a> meteor shower! Up to 100 meteors per hour are set to be visible in the northern hemisphere tonight \U0001f4ab\U0001f320\U0001f929 <a href="https://t.co/03MkV1cB4p">pic.twitter.com/03MkV1cB4p</a></p>, <p>\n<b>What\u2019s in a name?</b>\n</p>, <p>\ufeffThe Quadrantids are named for a constellation that no longer exists, according to\xa0<a href="https://earthsky.org/astronomy-essentials/everything-you-need-to-know-quadrantid-meteor-shower" shape="rect" target="_blank">EarthSky.org</a>. The name actually comes from the constellation Quadrans Muralis or Mural Quadrant, which was located between constellations Bootes the Herdsman and Draco the Dragon, near the end of the\xa0\u201cBig Dipper\u201d handle.</p>, <p>\xbb\xa0<a href="https://www.ajc.com/news/national/nasa-spacecraft-nears-asteroid-hoping-learn-secrets-early-solar-system/Pmr3Cf8k0KIdzV7uzDCwXP/" shape="rect">RELATED: NASA spacecraft nears asteroid hoping to learn secrets of early solar system</a>\n</p>, <p>\n<b>What causes the meteor shower?</b>\n</p>, <p>According to\xa0<a href="https://www.space.com/34373-orionid-meteor-shower-guide.html" shape="rect">NASA</a>, the meteor\u2019s particles originate from asteroid 2003 EH1, a now-extinct or \u201crock comet\u201d that takes 5.52 years to orbit the sun once. It was first discovered in 2003.</p>, <p>\u201cIt was either a piece of a comet or a comet itself, and then it became extinct,\u201d NASA meteor expert Bill Cooke told\xa0<a href="https://www.space.com/35142-quadrantid-meteor-shower-guide.html" shape="rect" target="_blank">Space.com</a>, meaning the comet\u2019s ice and other volatiles have evaporated, the site reported.</p>, <p>Experts also believe the asteroid has some connection to the Comet 96P/Machholtz, which orbits the sun every six years.</p>, <p>\n<a href="http://www.ajc.com/news/national/perseids-light-the-night-sky-annual-celestial-show-for-stargazers/zwojzmNo3cJs8dFfSP1xsI/" shape="rect">\xbb RELATED: Perseids light up the night sky in annual celestial show for stargazers</a>\n</p>, <p>\n<b>How many meteors will I see?</b>\n<br/>\n</p>, <p>During the shower\u2019s narrow peak, you may be able to see up to 60 to 200 \u201c bright fireball meteors\u201d per hour under perfect conditions. But it\u2019s likely you\u2019ll miss many of the fainter meteors.</p>, <p>The shower\u2019s \u201cfireballs are larger explosions of light and color that can persist longer than an average meteor streak,\u201d according to NASA. \u201cThis is due to the fact that fireballs originate from larger particles of material.\u201d</p>, <p>\n<br/>\xbb\xa0<a href="https://www.ajc.com/lifestyles/recreation/georgia-state-park-named-one-world-top-stargazing-spots/rKHnYjPJiXgkIOGZR1YNhL/" shape="rect">RELATED: Georgia state park named one of world\u2019s top stargazing spots</a>\n</p>, <p>\n<b>When will it peak?</b>\n</p>, <p>According to the\xa0<a href="https://www.imo.net/files/meteor-shower/cal2019.pdf" shape="rect">International Meteor Organization</a>, the shower will peak at 2 a.m. UTC (9 p.m. on Jan. 3 EST). Skygazers in Europe are likely to get the best views,\xa0\u201cbut viewers in North America might catch a few Quadrantids in the ramp-up to the peak,\u201d Cooke told\xa0<a href="https://www.space.com/35142-quadrantid-meteor-shower-guide.html" shape="rect" target="_blank">Space.com</a>.</p>, <p>\n<b>Where do I have to go to watch the meteor showers?</b>\n</p>, <p>The meteor shower will be visible from the Northern Hemisphere, and best viewed from mid-northern and far-northern latitudes. NASA experts recommend finding an area well away from city or street lights for optimal darkness.</p>, <p>\n<a href="http://www.ajc.com/news/national/photos-perseid-meteor-shower-brightens-the-night-sky/r8KJndGgTDiIpl0JmHFycN/" shape="rect">\xbb RELATED: Photos: Perseid meteor shower brightens the night sky</a>\n</p>, <p>\n<b>Do I need binoculars?</b>\n</p>, <p>According to\xa0<a href="https://www.space.com/34373-orionid-meteor-shower-guide.html" shape="rect" target="_blank">Space.com</a>, binoculars and telescopes won\u2019t help. That\u2019s because those tools are designed to magnify and focus on stationary objects in the sky.</p>, <p>The naked eye will do just fine.</p>, <p>\n<b>How to safely watch the shower</b>\n</p>, <p>\n<a href="https://solarsystem.nasa.gov/asteroids-comets-and-meteors/meteors-and-meteorites/quadrantids/in-depth/" shape="rect" target="_blank">Some advice from NASA</a>: \u201cCome prepared for winter weather with a sleeping bag, blanket or lawn chair. Lie flat on your back with your feet facing northeast and look up, taking in as much of the sky as possible. In less than 30 minutes in the dark, your eyes will adapt and you will begin to see meteors. Be patient\u2014the show will last until dawn, so you have plenty of time to catch a glimpse.\u201d</p>, <p>\n<a href="http://www.accessatlanta.com/events/outdoors--recreation/nature/eerie-awe-inspiring-ways-explore-georgia-new-dark-sky-park/BeYXvUQct9c2yrq2XWCliO/" shape="rect">\xbb RELATED: Eerie, awe-inspiring: 5 ways to explore Georgia's new Dark Sky Park</a>\n</p>, <p class="p">\xa9 2018\xa0<a href="http://www.coxmediagroup.com" shape="rect" target="_blank">Cox Media Group</a></p>]
[<p>Supported by</p>, <p class="css-16vrk19 e1x1pwtg1" itemid="" itemprop="author creator" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">By<!-- --> <a class="css-1riqqik e1x1pwtg0" href="https://www.nytimes.com/by/steven-lee-myers"><span class="css-1baulvz" itemprop="name">Steven Lee Myers</span></a></p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">BEIJING \u2014 Hours after a space probe from China made humanity\u2019s <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/02/world/asia/china-change-4-moon.html?action=click&amp;module=inline&amp;pgtype=Homepage" title="">first landing on the far side of the moon</a>, sending images of its surroundings back to Earth, the spacecraft deployed a rover on Thursday to take still more photographs and scan the surface of terrain never before traversed.</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">The rover, weighing 300 pounds, rolled off a ramp on the lander at 10:22 p.m. Beijing time, laying deep tracks in the moon\u2019s soft soil, its solar panels spread like wings, according to a photograph released to state media. The rover is now programmed to roam across a barren vista toward a distinct crater.</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">Chinese scientists hailed the landing of the Chang\u2019e-4 probe as evidence of the country\u2019s growing stature in space exploration. \u201cIt is human nature to explore the unknown world,\u201d Wu Weiren, chief designer of the lunar mission for the China National Space Administration, said in an interview on the state television network, CCTV. \u201cAnd it is what our generation and the next generation are supposed to do.\u201d</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">Compared with previous missions, however, the reaction to Thursday\u2019s milestones seemed strikingly restrained, both in the country\u2019s state-run news outlets and on social media. On China\u2019s most-watched TV news program early Thursday evening, the landing \u2014 declared a success by officials at mission control \u2014 was not even one of the four top stories.</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">The doodle of China\u2019s biggest search engine, <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="http://www.baidu.com/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank" title="">Baidu</a>, paid subtle homage to the lander and its rover, but the news was relegated to the fifth item on CCTV\u2019s 7 p.m. news program. It followed three reports on the doings of the country\u2019s leader, Xi Jinping, and an item on a new government zone being developed outside Beijing. In interviews, several people said they had paid little attention to the moon landing.</p>, <p class="css-1uuihdo">China\u2019s Chang\u2019e-4 became the first spacecraft to make a soft landing on the far side of the moon.</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0"><em class="css-2fg4z9 ehxkw330">[Why China\u2019s </em><a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/02/world/asia/china-change-4-moon.html?action=click&amp;module=inline&amp;pgtype=Article" title=""><em class="css-2fg4z9 ehxkw330">moon landing</em></a><em class="css-2fg4z9 ehxkw330"> was hailed a \u2018new chapter in humanity\u2019s exploration of the moon.\u2019]</em></p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">The muted reaction was a sign that the novelty of the country\u2019s space missions has faded. But the coverage also appeared to reflect political and economic anxieties at a time when Mr. Xi\u2019s government is trying to negotiate a truce in the trade war with the United States and respond to worrisome cracks in the economy.</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">A woman in a cafe in Beijing, Liu Ying, expressed pride in the space program but said she had not followed the landing closely. She then expressed wonder about the costs. \u201cThe economy is bad,\u201d she said. \u201cIs it really a good thing for the country to spend recklessly?\u201d</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">The government does not disclose how much it spends on its space programs, but it has made it clear that this launch was part of an ambitious goal to <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2018/05/23/world/asia/china-space-moon.html?module=inline" title="">establish China as one of the world\u2019s space powers</a>, rivaling the United States. Officials have said the country hopes to establish a lunar base that could provide natural resources for the Earth but also serve as a launching pad for further exploration.</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">The first of three photographs sent by Chang\u2019e-4 appeared a little over an hour after the spacecraft <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/02/world/asia/china-change-4-moon.html?module=inline" title="">touched down</a> as planned at 10:26 a.m., Beijing time, in the middle of a crater not far from the moon\u2019s south pole. It showed a barren, undulating vista pocked by a smaller crater, as did another picture sent 12 hours later as the rover began its journey.</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">Contrary to t<a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/02/science/far-side-moon.html?module=inline" title="">he enduring but mistaken notion that the moon has a \u201cdark side\u201d</a> \u2014 you can blame <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-features/pink-floyds-dark-side-of-the-moon-10-things-you-didnt-know-201743/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank" title="">Pink Floyd</a> for that, at least in part \u2014 the photographs showed the landscape bathed in an orange hue, casting the sharp shadows from the lander and the rover. The other two, in black and white, showed the lander descending.</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">The spacecraft was the first to land intact on the side of the moon that perpetually faces away from Earth. A Soviet satellite took the first photographs of the far side in 1959, and the Apollo missions circled above it between 1968 and 1972, but the difficulty of communicating with earthbound scientists had always made the idea of landing there more complex, if not necessarily prohibitive.</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">Dr. Wu, in his televised remarks, said the landing had been a \u201cgreat kickoff\u201d for future lunar missions, including ones intended to land astronauts \u2014 something only the United States has accomplished, sending 12 men to the moon. Under the current schedule, China would send the first astronaut by 2030.</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">\u201cWe are building China into a space giant,\u201d he said.</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">To overcome the challenge of communicating from the moon\u2019s far side, China had previously launched a satellite called Queqiao, or Magpie Bridge. It now orbits beyond the moon to act as a relay for transmissions to and from the mission control center on the northwestern outskirts of Beijing.</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">China\u2019s first lunar probe, known as Chang\u2019e-3, <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2013/12/15/world/asia/china-lands-probe-on-the-moon-report-says.html?module=inline" title="">landed on the near side of the moon in 2013</a>. It also released a rover, but it was hindered by terrain and communication problems. After a month it came to a halt, and broadcast only intermittently following that.</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">Yu Guobin, a spokesman for the Chang\u2019e-4 program, said in televised remarks that the detachment of the rover was the \u201cmore important historical moment.\u201d</p>, <p class="css-1ygdjhk e2kc3sl0">NASA\u2019s administrator, Jim Bridenstine, congratulated his Chinese counterparts for the successful landing. In a message on Twitter, he called the mission \u201ca first for humanity <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://twitter.com/JimBridenstine/status/1080678873422016513" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank" title="">and an impressive accomplishment</a>!\u201d Twitter is banned inside China\u2019s Great Firewall, but his remark was widely quoted nonetheless.</p>, <p>Zoe Mou and Claire Fu contributed research.</p>, <p><em>Follow Steven Lee Myers on Twitter: <a href="https://twitter.com/stevenleemyers">@stevenleemyers</a>.</em></p>, <p class="css-19n3nxx etcg8100"></p>, <p class="css-19n3nxx etcg8100"></p>, <p class="css-19n3nxx etcg8100"></p>, <p>Advertisement</p>]
[<p>While flying by Jupiter in late December 2018, NASA\u2019s Juno spacecraft captured <a class="E" href="https://www.sciencedaily.com/releases/2019/01/190102112852.htm" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">new pictures of volcanic plumes on Jupiter\u2019s moon</a> Io. The pictures are being touted by scientists as \u201cone of the best images of Io\u201d Juno\u2019s cameras have captured to date. Happy new year! Look at some cool pictures of volcanoes 365 million miles away from Earth!</p>, <p>The images were taken on Dec. 21, during winter solstice. During the spacecraft\u2019s 17th flyby of the planet, four of Juno\u2019s cameras took images of Jupiter\u2019s moon Io, which a <a class="E" href="https://www.swri.org/press-release/light-from-volcanoes-io-juno-jupiter-moon" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">press release</a> from Southwest Research Institute calls \u201cthe most volcanic body in our solar system.\u201d Io\u2019s volcanoes were initially discovered by NASA's Voyager spacecraft almost 40 years ago, in 1979. However, these newest pictures are giving scientists a clearer image of the the volcanic activity on Io.</p>, <p>\u201cWe knew we were breaking new ground with a multi-spectral campaign to view Io\u2019s polar region, but no one expected we would get so lucky as to see an active volcanic plume shooting material off the moon's surface,\u201d Scott Bolton, principal investigator of the Juno mission and an associate vice president of Southwest Research Institute\u2019s Space Science and Engineering Division, said in the press release. \u201cThis is quite a New Year\u2019s present showing us that Juno has the ability to clearly see plumes.\u201d</p>, <p>That settles it: 2019 is the year of volcanic plumes. </p>, <p>Juno observed Jupiter\u2019s moon for over an hour, capturing the images which show evidence of an active eruption. To the non-scientific eye, the above photo may just look like darkness, blurry light, bits of yellow and orange. However, as the press release explains, there\u2019s actually a lot going on in the picture: \u201cThe brightest feature on Io in the image is thought to be a penetrating radiation signature, a reminder of this satellite's role in feeding Jupiter's radiation belts, while other features show the glow of activity from several volcanoes\u201d</p>, <p>Why was Juno able to capture the volcanic activity? In part, because they\u2019re illuminated by the nearby moon Europa. In part, because of just how big the plumes are. As Candice Hansen-Koharcheck, the JunoCam lead from the Planetary Science Institute, explains, \u201cThe ground is already in shadow, but the height of the plume allows it to reflect sunlight, much like the way mountaintops or clouds on the Earth continue to be lit after the sun has set.\u201d </p>, <p>Those two things combined with Juno\u2019s low-light cameras made for an ideal opportunity to capture these new images. \u201cAs a low-light camera designed to track the stars, the SRU can only observe Io under very dimly lit conditions,\u201d Heidi Becker, lead of Juno's Radiation Monitoring Investigation, at NASA's Jet Propulsion Laboratory. said. \u201cDec. 21 gave us a unique opportunity to observe Io's volcanic activity with the SRU using only Europa's moonlight as our lightbulb.\u201d </p>, <p>Basically, ideal lighting and good timing are to thank for these now-historic pictures.</p>, <p>Juno launched in 2011 and first arrived at Jupiter in 2016. The craft is now halfway through its mission, with scientists aiming Juno to complete its map of Jupiter by mid-2021. \u201cThough Jupiter's moons are not JIRAM's primary objectives, every time we pass close enough to one of them, we take advantage of the opportunity for an observation,\u201d Alberto Adriani, a researcher at Italy's National Institute of Astrophysics, said. \u201cThe instrument is sensitive to infrared wavelengths, which are perfect to study the volcanism of Io. This is one of the best images of Io that JIRAM has been able to collect so far.\u201d</p>, <p>So, what does this all mean to us earthbound beings? For starters, These new images will also help scientists better understand how Jupiter interacts with its five moons and the phenomena it causes, like Io\u2019s volcanoes.</p>, <p>If planetary meanings are your thing, perhaps you could look into <a class="E" href="https://www.bustle.com/p/what-does-it-mean-if-jupiter-is-in-sagittarius-this-planet-brings-good-luck-to-all-zodiac-signs-13206069">how Jupiter affects your zodiac sign</a>. The giant gas planet is moving into Sagittarius, which is thought to bring good luck. There was certainly a bit of good cosmic timing in play when Juno captured its latest pictures.</p>]

[<p>2018 was a quiet year for Olympus, but the Micro Four Thirds company will start 2019 with the launch of what appears to be a high-end camera geared toward sports photographers. Olympus released a teaser video for an unnamed OM-D camera with a launch date of January 24.</p>, <p>The 18-second teaser reveals little about the upcoming camera save for a few glimpses of the body and the situations in which it\u2019s apparently meant to excel. While the camera is unnamed, the video does end on the OM-D logo, suggesting it could be a replacement to the <a href="https://www.digitaltrends.com/digital-camera-reviews/olympus-om-d-e-m1-mark-ii-review/">OM-D E-M1 Mark II</a> that\u2019s going on three years old.</p>, <p>A silhouette of the camera shows a body that appears to be a bit taller than a typical OM-D or has a battery grip accessory attached. But what perhaps offers more clues to the new OM-D is <i>where</i> the camera is. The teaser shows the camera shooting at several different sports events, including football, beach volleyball, and water polo, suggesting the camera is geared for sports action. This may also suggest professional level dust- and splash-proofing, something Olympus is already well known for.</p>, <p>While Panasonic, Nikon,\xa0and Canon announced full-frame mirrorless cameras last year, <a href="https://camerajabber.com/olympus-full-frame-is-good-for-micro-four-thirds/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">interviews with Olympus executives suggest</a> Olympus isn\u2019t planning on ditching the Micro Four Thirds format. The camera body certainly appears to be large enough to support a larger sensor, but sticking with Four Thirds would make sense. The smaller format smaller and lighter lenses, making extreme telephoto lenses easier to carry, which would certainly be welcome in sports photography.</p>, <p>Last year, Olympus had few product launches, with the <a href="https://www.digitaltrends.com/digital-camera-reviews/olympus-pen-e-pl9-review/">beginner-friendly E-PL9</a>\xa0being its most prominent. The company\u2019s OM-D line, on the other hand, is typically more pro-oriented. While more companies continue to push for higher resolution, larger sensors, Olympus\u2019 past launches have focused on other technologies, like image stabilization and advanced shooting modes, like Pro Capture and the High-Resolution Shot.</p>, <p>2019 also marks Olympus\u2019 100th anniversary \u2014 an important product launch would be a good way to mark the occasion. Olympus has <a href="https://www.getolympus.com/us/en/omdrevolution?SID=ifqpkeiqlbrf0mr8lhh8hmaui2" rel="noopener" target="_blank">a countdown to the launch set on its website</a>, along with an email sign-up to receive more details.</p>]
[<p>University of Maryland researchers have given Google a "welcome to 2019" gift by breaking its latest reCaptcha audio challenge.</p>, <p>The work is a follow-up to <a href="https://www.theregister.co.uk/2017/10/31/uncaptcha_research_cracks_audio_captchas/" target="_blank">an attack</a> published in April 2017 by the university's Kevin Bock, Daven Patel, George Hughey and Dave Levin, again attacking the audio challenges. Since then, Google has updated the code, and the boffins have updated their attack.</p>, <p>The audio challenge was created to solve reCaptcha's accessibility problem \u2013 someone using a screen reader can't see where to "tick the box" to prove they aren't a robot.</p>, <p>The 2017 attack, documented <a href="http://uncaptcha.cs.umd.edu/" target="_blank">here</a>, downloaded and segmented the audio captcha, sent the segments on to multiple online speech-to-text services, checked the responses for homophones, applied a weighted vote to those responses, and uploaded the answer to reCaptcha.</p>, <p>They claimed better than 85 per cent accuracy for that attack, and when Google fixed reCaptcha's audio challenge, the group set to work attacking the replacement. They demonstrated that the fixes made reCaptcha less secure, told Google in June 2018 (with a six-month disclosure deadline), and on Monday <a href="https://github.com/ecthros/uncaptcha2" target="_blank">published</a> unCaptcha2.</p>, <p>The group said: "Thanks to the changes to the audio challenge, [parsing] ReCaptcha is easier than ever before. The code now only needs to make a single request to a free, publicly available speech to text API to achieve around 90 per cent accuracy over all captchas."</p>, <p>The GitHub post notes that unCaptcha2 no longer needs to use multiple speech-to-text engines, and the fragmentation approach used in the first version has also been abandoned.</p>, <p>The boffins added that Google cleared them to release the code. "The Recaptcha team is aware of this attack vector, and have confirmed they are OK with us releasing this code, despite its current success rate."</p>, <p>They added: "While unCaptcha2 is tuned for Google's Demo site, it can be changed to work for any such site \u2013 the logic for defeating ReCaptcha will be the same."</p>, <p>Researchers wanting to check out unCaptcha2 for themselves will need their own API keys from the relevant services (speech-to-text engines from wit.ai, Bing, IBM and Google).</p>, <p>Since Google has had six months' notice, the boffins noted that unCaptcha2 could stop working at any time. \xae</p>, <p class="foot_desc"><strong>The Register</strong> - Independent news and views for the tech community. Part of Situation Publishing</p>, <p>Join our daily or weekly newsletters, subscribe to a specific section or set <a href="https://account.theregister.co.uk/alert/?create=1">News alerts</a></p>, <p>Biting the hand that feeds IT \xa9 1998\u20132019</p>]
[<p>You\u2019ll see a theme if you scroll back the last decade or so on <i><span style="font-weight: 400;">MO</span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;">: we have a thing for the Triumph Street Triple. After numerous rides and shootouts each time it gets updated, it\u2019s safe to say we love that little 675cc three-cylinder. The sound it makes is outrageously cool, the power it delivers is fun without being overwhelming, and the overall package is an absolute blast. Yeah, the looks are kinda polarizing, but none of that matters once you twist the grip.</span></p>, <p id="galleryPlayer_1"><a href="http://www.macromedia.com/go/getflashplayer">Get the Flash Player</a> to see this player.</p>, <p>Then, lo-and-behold, Triumph one-upped itself and upgraded the Street Triple at the end of 2017 as a 2018 model, giving it a significant bump in displacement: up to 765cc \u2013 much to the grins of dyslexics everywhere. Of course, the magic of three cylinders didn\u2019t go anywhere, and the new bike was once again a hit amongst us all. Tom \u201cBiceps\u201d Roderick seriously considered buying one when he walked out the proverbial <i>MO</i> door on his way to self-employment. Meanwhile, we all liked it enough to name it <a href="https://www.motorcycle.com/mobos/best-standard-motorcycle-2018.html"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Motorcycle.com\u2019s Best Standard Motorcycle of 2018</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. And by \u201cit\u201d I\u2019m talking about Triumph\u2019s top-of-the-range RS version of the Street Triple. Contenders for the Streetie\u2019s crown have come and gone, and while some have done better than others at swaying our opinion, at the end of the day our hearts have always gravitated back to the Triumph. </span></p>, <p>KTM\u2019s response? \u201cChallenge accepted.\u201d</p>, <p class="wp-caption-text">\u201cI see your Street Triple R, and I raise you this.\u201d -KTM</p>, <p>Okay, we seriously doubt this was actually said inside some KTM board meeting (although it\u2019d be great if it were), but when it comes to benchmarking an existing model for KTM\u2019s new 799cc parallel-Twin, Team Orange couldn\u2019t have picked a better target. Of course, we all know the result: the 790 Duke. Our European friends got to taste the Orange kool-aid a year before we did, but when Evans came back from his <a href="https://www.motorcycle.com/manufacturer/ktm/2019-ktm-790-duke-review-first-ride.html"><span style="font-weight: 400;">790 Duke First Ride</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> he really loved it \u2013 as in, he was thinking of ways to buy one without pissing off his wife. Naturally, our response was to put the KTM head-to-head with the Triumph to see if our favorite little Triple could hold off yet another challenger. If you need detailed overviews of each bike, click on the links above for a breakdown.</span></p>, <p>Naturally, we do our best to keep comparisons as fair as possible, and the basis of this starts with price. The 790 Duke only comes in one flavor with pricing set at $10,499. With that, you get a potent 799cc parallel-Twin \u2013 which, as you should know by now, is a first for KTM \u2013 pumping out 98.0 hp and 60.2 lb-ft to the rear wheel on the MotoGP Werks dyno. Accompanying the Twin is an electronics suite featuring adjustable (and switchable) traction control, ABS, power modes, and best of all, a quickshifter in both directions. Brakes are twin 300mm discs with J.Juan radial-mount 4-pot calipers in the front, 240mm single disc and one-pot J.Juan caliper in the back. WP handles suspension duties (pun not intended), but cheaps out a bit offering a non-adjustable 43mm fork and a shock with just preload settings available.</p>, <p class="wp-caption-text">If you look strictly at the numbers, the Triumph wins the horsepower war. Look closer and you\u2019ll see it\u2019s only after the KTM signs off that the Street Triple gets its advantage.</p>, <p>The Street Triple, however, comes in a variety of flavors, from the $9,950 S model on up to the $12,550 RS. While the latter gets all the bells and whistles like a quickshifter (only for upshifts), five ride modes, Brembo M50 calipers, \xd6hlins shock, and the most power in the range \u2013 a claimed 121 hp and 57 lb-ft \u2013 the price moves it rather far away from the KTM, especially considering the Triumph also comes in an R version starting at $11,250 \u2013 much more in line with the 790. For that price, the R gets Brembo M4.32 calipers, Showa Big Piston fork and adjustable shock, four ride modes (no Track mode), full TFT instrumentation, and slightly less power than the RS \u2013 ours put down 114.9 hp and 56.7 lb-ft to the wheel, according to the MotoGP Werks dyno.</p>, <p>However, things aren\u2019t always as perfect as they seem, since we were sent the R model in the Matt Aluminum Silver color, adding $250 extra, for a total of $11,500. A whole thousand bucks more than the KTM. To confuse matters that much more, the base Street Triple S version starts at $9,950 and moves up to $10,200. While that may be the closest from a cost perspective, the S model is slightly detuned from the R (which is already a little down to the RS), only gets two riding modes, lower-spec Showa suspension, and basic pin-slide two-piston Nissin brakes. Neither the R or S gets a quickshifter, but going on cost and which features most closely line up, we opted for the Street Triple R to face the 790 Duke.</p>, <p class="wp-caption-text">The picture looks even worse for the Triumph in the torque department, where the KTM has its number. Just look at that advantage in the midrange \u2013 although the Triumph\u2019s fueling does look much cleaner.</p>, <p>The procedure is fairly simple from here: we flog them on the street, then rinse and repeat at the track, joining our friends at <a href="https://www.rickdiculousracing.com/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Rickdiculous Racing</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> for a day at Chuckwalla. Keeping with the apples-to-apples theme, we spooned each bike with </span><a href="https://www.motorcycle.com/products/dunlop-sportmax-q4-review"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Dunlop\u2019s Q4 tire</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. We did this for a few reasons. First, the Q4 is a track-focused tire for the road rider, meaning it can handle street riding just fine, but it also heats up quickly for track use without the need for warmers \u2013 perfect for us lazy </span><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">MO</span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;">rons who don\u2019t want to bother with slapping blankets on tires after each session. Second, and maybe more importantly, the standard tires on our test Triumph were already squared off in the center from a previous user. That would have impacted handling severely and unfairly against the ST765. \xa0</span></p>, <p>Considering my time aboard the <a href="https://www.motorcycle.com/manufacturer/kramer/world-exclusive-kramer-gp2-prototype-first-ride.html"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Kramer GP2 Prototype</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, powered by the same 799cc Twin as the KTM, I was anxious to see how the 790 Duke would perform. Joining me on this flog-a-thon is none other than \u201cBiceps\u201d Roderick, coaxed out of semi-retirement by the call of a wailing Triple and a burbling Twin (and the offer of a free breakfast). But since he was on the verge of actually buying a Street Triple, Tom was the perfect candidate.</span></p>, <p class="wp-caption-text">We opted to run the Dunlop Q4 tires on both bikes for a few reasons, but mainly because we didn\u2019t want to use tire warmers at the racetrack.</p>, <p>Looking at the specs (and considering our past experience), on paper the Triumph appeared to be better of the two. With three cylinders, more power, and only a nine-pound weight difference on the official <em>MO</em> scales (420 lbs vs. 411 for the KTM), both Tom and I had a hard time imagining the Triumph losing. Out on the road, the Streetie exhibited all of its lovable character, too. The three-cylinder wail is as intoxicating as ever, and now that it has more displacement, the extra shove when you twist your wrist adds to the excitement factor. Not having a quickshifter was a bit of a drag, but that\u2019s a first-world problem if ever there were one. The Streetie shifts just fine if you know what you\u2019re doing, and the slipper clutch does a great job of keeping the rear in check if you don\u2019t. Adjustable levers and an informative TFT display, including gear indicator, are also a nice touch.</p>, <p>If the specs and the dyno numbers were all we needed to determine these tests, then our job would be incredibly easy (and boring). Sometimes though, the magic can\u2019t be found on a piece of paper. This is the beauty of the KTM 790 Duke. Despite what the numbers say, both Tom and I fell for the 790 instantly. KTM dubs the bigger 1290 Super Duke R \u201cThe Beast\u201d and this, the 790 Duke, \u201cThe Scalpel\u201d \u2013 and after riding it, the name definitely fits. The smaller Duke takes the attitude of the big, burly 1290 and refines it to a precision-like quality with the 790.</p>, <p><a href="https://www.motorcycle.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/010219-2019-KTM-790-Duke-Triumph-Street-Triple-Group-Action_EBB6291.jpg"><img alt="" class="alignnone size-large wp-image-93713" height="388" sizes="(max-width: 633px) 100vw, 633px" src="https://www.motorcycle.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/010219-2019-KTM-790-Duke-Triumph-Street-Triple-Group-Action_EBB6291-633x388.jpg" srcset="https://www.motorcycle.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/010219-2019-KTM-790-Duke-Triumph-Street-Triple-Group-Action_EBB6291-633x388.jpg 633w, https://www.motorcycle.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/010219-2019-KTM-790-Duke-Triumph-Street-Triple-Group-Action_EBB6291-768x471.jpg 768w, https://www.motorcycle.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/010219-2019-KTM-790-Duke-Triumph-Street-Triple-Group-Action_EBB6291-75x46.jpg 75w, https://www.motorcycle.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/010219-2019-KTM-790-Duke-Triumph-Street-Triple-Group-Action_EBB6291-120x74.jpg 120w, https://www.motorcycle.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/010219-2019-KTM-790-Duke-Triumph-Street-Triple-Group-Action_EBB6291-150x93.jpg 150w, https://www.motorcycle.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/010219-2019-KTM-790-Duke-Triumph-Street-Triple-Group-Action_EBB6291-186x114.jpg 186w, https://www.motorcycle.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/010219-2019-KTM-790-Duke-Triumph-Street-Triple-Group-Action_EBB6291-210x128.jpg 210w, https://www.motorcycle.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/010219-2019-KTM-790-Duke-Triumph-Street-Triple-Group-Action_EBB6291-224x137.jpg 224w, https://www.motorcycle.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/010219-2019-KTM-790-Duke-Triumph-Street-Triple-Group-Action_EBB6291-270x165.jpg 270w, https://www.motorcycle.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/010219-2019-KTM-790-Duke-Triumph-Street-Triple-Group-Action_EBB6291-408x250.jpg 408w, https://www.motorcycle.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/010219-2019-KTM-790-Duke-Triumph-Street-Triple-Group-Action_EBB6291-637x390.jpg 637w" width="633"/></a></p>, <p>Despite having one less cylinder than the Triumph, Tom was convinced this is \u201cprobably one of the best parallel-twin engines ever! The Trumpet may make more peak horsepower, but look for yourself at the dyno chart and see how the KTM\u2019s Twin romps the Triumph\u2019s Triple from 3,100 rpm to 9,100 rpm in horsepower production, while also producing significantly more torque through the same rev range. And the dyno data can be felt in the real world whether on the street or at the track.\u201d</p>, <p>This is the secret sauce behind the KTM. While the Triumph makes more power, it\u2019s only after the KTM hits redline that the 765 Triple shines, meaning you have to wind it up to keep chase. At Chuckwalla this wasn\u2019t much of an issue, since you naturally keep engines singing at the track \u2013 and in fact the Triumph easily kept the KTM in its dust when it came to outright speed. But when you\u2019re cruising the street or even playing in the canyons, the broad spread of power from the Duke is easier to tap into.</p>, <p class="wp-caption-text">The heart of the KTM 790 Duke is this 799cc parallel-Twin engine that punches way above its weight.</p>, <p>Of course, since the KTM has a smaller rev window compared to the Triumph, you also have to shift more. Not a problem, since the Duke not only has a quickshifter, but it works for both up- and down-shifts \u2013 not bad for $10,5K. That said, the QS isn\u2019t the slickest system in the world. Downshifts are a little clunky at times, and if I really wanted to go from sixth to third quickly I\u2019d resort to using the clutch. Still, it\u2019s nice to have.</p>, <p>\u201cEqually impressive to its power production is the KTM\u2019s handling,\u201d Tom says. \u201cEager to get leaned into a corner, the KTM holds its trajectory and absorbs road imperfections surprisingly well for a bike with non-adjustable suspension units.\u201d It\u2019s true. Despite its basic suspension bits, we never found ourselves eagerly wishing to adjust settings at either end on the KTM, even at the track. Could they be better? Sure, slightly stiffer springs and/or increased damping wouldn\u2019t hurt.</p>, <p class="wp-caption-text">When given room to stretch its legs, the KTM only gets smaller in the Triumph\u2019s mirrors.</p>, <p>The biggest surprise by far is how each motorcycle carries its weight. As T-Rod explains, \u201cWhat doesn\u2019t translate from paper to real world is the KTM\u2019s seemingly minor nine-pound weight advantage. I\u2019m still scratching my head at how KTM managed to make the 790 Duke feel 50 pounds lighter than the Street Triple. Whatever magic combination of CoG, rake, trail and wheelbase numbers works so well I just can\u2019t believe it\u2019s not butter.\u201d</p>, <p>As if this test didn\u2019t bring us a few surprises already, what continually left us floored was how much lighter the 790 feels. It\u2019s worth saying it again \u2013 the KTM is only nine pounds lighter than the Triumph \u2013 but whether on the street or the track, hustling each bike from side to side was dramatically different. The Street Triple feels slow and lethargic (words we\u2019d never otherwise use to describe the ST) compared to the quickness and agility of the 790 Duke. It\u2019s otherworldly.</p>, <p class="wp-caption-text">Screw what the scales say. You really need to ride the two back-to-back to understand how much lighter the KTM feels compared to the Triumph.</p>, <p>On the electronics front, both are equipped with TC and ABS. At the track, both ABS systems intervene earlier than prefered, the Triumph especially so, leading me to shut them off. The Duke does come with a Supermoto ABS setting, letting you lock the rear wheel to your heart\u2019s content. That said, Tom and I are split about which brakes we prefer. Personally, I lean towards the feel and power of the Triumph\u2019s Brembos while Tom\u2019s on the KTM\u2019s side. The TC nod also goes to the KTM, as it\u2019s adjustable to different levels, and performs remarkably well at putting the power down without too much distraction to the rider. Once slip is noticed on the Street Triple R, power is cut dramatically. And there\u2019s only on or off, no selecting of different levels.</p>, <p>Turning our attention away from flogging and onto slogging \u2013 as in, casual riding \u2013 things look a little better for the Triumph. First, \u201cthe Triumph has a much cushier seat compared to the KTM\u2019s flat, densely-cushioned pad,\u201d says Tom. \u201cBut the extra legroom on the Duke and more upright riding position kept me happier during freeway riding.\u201d Personally, I appreciated the KTM\u2019s extra legroom, but the upright seating position left me feeling like a sail on the highway. Without any wind protection, I preferred the Triumph\u2019s slight forward lean to help offset the windblast.</p>, <p class="wp-caption-text">If the KTM 790 Duke didn\u2019t exist, we\u2019d continue to be singing the Triumph\u2019s praises. In fact, if we had the RS to play with our opinions might be different.</p>, <p>This is one of those rare times when we don\u2019t need the MO scorecard to pick a winner. If you\u2019ve read this far it should seem fairly obvious. It\u2019s just surprising to us that it happened with these bikes. At first, we thought the Triumph had an easy win lined up for itself. Turns out the reality was entirely different. Let Tom clarify:</p>, <p><i>\u201cThere\u2019s really nothing to complain about when it comes to the Triumph. It\u2019s still the same excellent motorcycle with all qualities we love that catapulted it to the top of MO\u2019s 2018 Best Standard category. It\u2019s only when ridden back-to-back with the Duke that it becomes apparent how much heavier and lethargic the ST3 is compared to the new Duke. However, maybe I\u2019d change my tune if it were the RS model for $2,000 more.</i></p>, <p><i>For the $1k price difference, and considering all the other previously mentioned reasons, it\u2019s easy to chose the KTM over the Triumph. With the money saved a person can then go about upgrading the KTM\u2019s only real flaw (if you want to call it that) \u2014 it\u2019s non-adjustable suspension components.\u201d</i></p>, <p class="wp-caption-text">We have a new crush in the middleweight category. And it\u2019s Austrian.</p>]

[<p>As much as <a href="https://thetakeout.com/lacroix-ingredients-lawsuit-linalool-pesticides-1829553548" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'External link', 'https://thetakeout.com/lacroix-ingredients-lawsuit-linalool-pesticides-1829553548', {metric25:1})" rel="nofollow">I love LaCroix</a>, there is one flavor I\u2019ve never been able to stomach. Even worse to me than the blue \u201cnothing\u201d flavor is LaCroix coconut. It sounds like it should be tasty and satisfying, but in fact tastes like the tincture of suntan oil brewed over the La Brea tar pits. Every once in awhile I forget and will find a can laying around at work, and think, \u201coh, I should try this again.\u201d Every single time I regret this decision. A better descriptive name on this can than \u201cCoconut\u201d would be \u201cTropical Dirt.\u201d<br/></p>, <p>So I was somewhat understandably wary of another coconut flavor that recently crossed my desk, from the <a href="http://www.newyorkseltzer.com/" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'External link', 'http://www.newyorkseltzer.com/', {metric25:1})" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Original New York Seltzer Company</a>. But these guys get it. I have a fondness for <a href="https://thetakeout.com/blind-taste-test-best-lime-seltzer-sparkling-water-1828695766" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'External link', 'https://thetakeout.com/blind-taste-test-best-lime-seltzer-sparkling-water-1828695766', {metric25:1})" rel="nofollow">LaCroix Key Lime flavor</a> because it somehow tastes like cream pie. <em>All</em> the New York Seltzer flavors are like that. The orange tastes like a dreamsicle, and the coconut is what I wished the LaCroix coconut would have been. It\u2019s like a coconut cream pie in a can: creamy, sweet, and somehow completely indulgent when it doesn\u2019t have a single calorie or carb. (Even its more indulgent <a href="http://www.newyorkseltzer.com/classic/#1489553033976-9d2d6af2-c688" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'External link', 'http://www.newyorkseltzer.com/classic/#1489553033976-9d2d6af2-c688', {metric25:1})" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Vanilla Cream Soda</a> tastes like an <a href="https://thetakeout.com/whats-a-chocolate-egg-cream-1828711730" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'External link', 'https://thetakeout.com/whats-a-chocolate-egg-cream-1828711730', {metric25:1})" rel="nofollow">egg cream</a>.) </p>, <p>As it\u2019s <a href="https://thetakeout.com/consider-dryuary-alcohol-free-january-1831342632" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'External link', 'https://thetakeout.com/consider-dryuary-alcohol-free-january-1831342632', {metric25:1})" rel="nofollow">Dryuary</a>, and I am on my now-annual search for excellent non-alcoholic beverages, New York Seltzer would be at the top of my list, and its coconut flavor would be at the top of <em>that</em> list. Maybe with a splash of lemonade? A shot of mango juice? Sure, but it\u2019s also dessert-worthy enough on its own self, right out of the can, with solid coconut flavor that tastes more like a macaroon than soil from the inner layers of the earth.</p>, <p>Maybe this stems from my teenage past as a high school lifeguard, but there\u2019s something about coconut that evokes summer, spring break, and tropical climes, which makes the flavor a continual draw for me, beverage-wise\u2014especially during this bleak time of year. Short of a pi\xf1a colada (even a virgin pi\xf1a colada), Original New York Seltzer Coconut fits the bill perfectly, at a beverage height that LaCroix Coconut, stuck in its muddy tar pits, can only dream of reaching.</p>, <p class="author-bio__bio">Gwen Ihnat is deputy managing editor of The Takeout and a staff writer for The A.V. Club.</p>]
[<p>As 2019 gets underway, we\u2019re beginning to see the flood of year-end sales statistics from automakers. We\u2019ll have a few 2018-in-review pieces coming, but right now our focus is on American muscle. The U.S. sales figures are in for the 2018 <a href="https://www.motor1.com/chevrolet/camaro/" target="_self">Chevrolet Camaro</a>, 2018 <a href="https://www.motor1.com/ford/mustang/" target="_self">Ford Mustang</a>, and 2018 <a href="https://www.motor1.com/dodge/challenger/" target="_self">Dodge Challenger</a>, and for one of these cars, the news is quite grim.</p>, <p>We\u2019ll lead with the sales leader, and that title\xa0goes once again to the Ford Mustang. The original Pony Car is still the favorite among U.S. buyers by a significant margin, with 75,842 \u2018Stangs sold for the year. 2018 was the first full year for the car\u2019s mid-cycle facelift, not to mention the launch of the new<a href="https://www.motor1.com/news/227235/2019-mustang-bullitt-street-detroit/" target="_self"> Bullitt</a> but not all the news is good. Despite holding the top spot with ease, Mustang sales are actually down 7.4 percent compared to 2017.</p>, <p>We\u2019ve heard some disapproving comments from the Mustang community about the car\u2019s new front clip, or perhaps buyers are awaiting the new <a href="https://www.motor1.com/ford/shelby-gt500/" target="_self">GT500</a> which will<a href="https://www.motor1.com/news/280215/mustang-shelby-gt500-teaser/" target="_self"> debut in just a couple weeks</a> at the Detroit Auto Show. In any case, we suspect the year-over-year drop has the attention of Dearborn executives at the very least.</p>, <p>Also grabbing their attention \u2013 not to mention the high-level suits at FCA headquarters on the other side of Detroit in Auburn Hills \u2013 is Dodge Challenger sales. Despite a platform that\u2019s now a decade old, sales for the big muscle car are <em>up</em>. 66,716 Challengers found new homes last year, a rise of 3 percent compared to 2017. It\u2019s not much of an increase, but it\u2019s the only car among the three to post a year-over-year gain.</p>, <p>Credit<a href="https://www.motor1.com/dodge/" target="_self"> Dodge</a> for continually offering interesting packages to keep the old Challenger relevant among competition that\u2019s seen several major revisions in the same time frame. We also suspect the bonkers <a href="https://www.motor1.com/dodge/challenger-srt-demon/" target="_self">Challenger SRT Demon</a>\xa0performed well not just at the drag strip, but in dealerships as a halo car.\xa0</p>, <p>That leaves us with the 2018 Chevrolet Camaro, and as you can guess by now, this is where the news isn\u2019t so good. Despite offering perhaps the best Pony Car among the three on this list, Camaro sales fell through the floor last year. Only 50,963 were sold, representing a <em>25 percent drop</em> from the previous year. Like the Mustang, the Camaro entered 2018 with a facelift but it was widely criticized \u2013 so much in fact that <a href="https://www.motor1.com/chevrolet/" target="_self">Chevrolet</a> is<a href="https://www.motor1.com/news/273007/2020-camaro-ss-facelift/" target="_self"> fast-tracking a new front fascia to production</a>.</p>, <p>That\u2019s too bad, because in our comparison tests we loved nearly everything about the Camaro versus the competition, especially its driving dynamics. Here\u2019s hoping the new front fascia brings buyers back to Chevy showrooms, or else the fabled car could disappear from the lineup completely as it did in 2002.</p>, <p><em><strong>Source:</strong> GM, Ford, FCA</em></p>, <p><strong>DEARBORN, Mich., Jan. 3, 2019</strong>\xa0\u2013 Ford Motor Company (NYSE: F) today reported its December 2018 U.S. sales results. Click\xa0here\xa0or visit media.ford.com to view the news release. Ford will begin its monthly sales call at 10 a.m. EDT this morning when Erich Merkle, Ford U.S. sales analyst, will host a conference call for the investment community and news media to discuss the results and related market trends. He will be joined by Mark LaNeve, Ford vice president, U.S. Marketing, Sales and Service, and Emily Kolinski Morris, Ford chief economist.</p>, <p>\xa0</p>, <p>*\xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0*\xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0*</p>, <p>*\xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 *\xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0 \xa0*</p>, <p><strong>DETROIT \u2013\xa0</strong>General Motors (NYSE: GM) announced today that it delivered 2,954,037 vehicles in 2018, including more than 1 million crossovers, almost 974,000 pickup trucks and more than 280,000 large SUVs.</p>, <p><a id="_Hlk534103069" name="_Hlk534103069"></a>\u201cWe have built the most successful pickup, SUV and crossover business in the industry and we gained considerable momentum in the fourth quarter of 2018 as dealers began delivering the all-new Chevrolet Silverado, GMC Sierra and Cadillac\xa0XT4,\u201d said Kurt McNeil, U.S. vice president, Sales Operations.</p>, <p>GM\u2019s fourth quarter deliveries totaled 785,229 units and the company\u2019s share of the industry\u2019s retail sales grew every month from October through December.</p>, <p>\u201cWe feel confident heading into 2019 because we have more major truck and crossover launches coming during the year and the U.S. economy is strong,\u201d McNeil added.\xa0</p>, <p><strong>GM delivers more than 1 million crossovers in the U.S. in 2018</strong></p>, <p>Total sales of all utility vehicles, including large SUVs, totaled 1,295,700, up 7\xa0percent. [<p class="summary" itemprop="description alternativeHeadline">While the new frontier of intelligent object detection can create amazing eye candy, it is also tackling the decades-old problem of simply being heard in a crowd.</p>, <p class="meta">\n                                   By <a data-omniture-track="moduleClick" data-omniture-track-data='{"moduleInfo": "byline-author", "pageType": "article"}' data-vanity-rewritten="true" href="/meet-the-team/us/ross-rubin/" itemprop="author" rel="author">Ross Rubin</a>\n            \n                    \n        \n                                        |            <time datetime="2019-01-03 20:59:00">January 3, 2019 -- 20:59 GMT (12:59 PST)</time>\n        \n                                                                                            | Topic: <a data-omniture-track="moduleClick" data-omniture-track-data='{"moduleInfo": "byline-topic", "pageType": "article"}' href="/topic/artificial-intelligence/">Artificial Intelligence</a>\n</p>, <p class="title">\n<a data-omniture-track="moduleClick" data-omniture-track-data='{"moduleInfo": "pinbox", "pageType": "article"}' href="https://www.zdnet.com/article/artificial-intelligence-in-the-real-world-what-can-it-actually-do/">\n                        Artificial intelligence in the real world: What can it actually do?\n                    </a>\n</p>, <p class="dek">What are the limits of AI? And how do you go from managing data points to injecting AI in the enterprise?</p>, <p class="read-more">\n<a data-omniture-track="moduleClick" data-omniture-track-data='{"moduleInfo": "pinbox", "pageType": "article"}' href="https://www.zdnet.com/article/artificial-intelligence-in-the-real-world-what-can-it-actually-do/">Read More</a>\n</p>, <p>The <a href="https://www.zdnet.com/article/qualcomm-announces-snapdragon-855-mobile-platform/" target="_blank">Snapdragon 855</a> (for smartphones) and <a href="https://www.zdnet.com/article/qualcomm-announces-7nm-snapdragon-8cx-for-extreme-always-connected-pc-performance/" target="_blank">Snapdragon 8cx</a> (for PCs) that Qualcomm announced at its Snapdragon Summit last month include big leaps in virtually every significant benchmark such as CPU and GPU performance. But in an age where few smartphone applications push the mobile experience forward, the company showed how AI enhancements can go well beyond the photo quality optimizations that have become widely implemented by leading smartphone vendors.</p>, <p><strong>Also:\xa0</strong><a href="https://www.zdnet.com/article/the-ai-chip-unicorn-that-is-about-to-revolutionize-everything-has-computational-graph-at-its-core/" target="_blank"><strong>The AI chip unicorn that's about to revolutionize everything</strong></a></p>, <p>The demonstrations -- promised to be only a hint of the kinds of wizardry AI can muster -- made some of the strongest cases to date about how <a href="https://www.zdnet.com/article/ai-startup-petuum-aims-to-industrialize-machine-learning/" target="_blank">AI-based computations</a> can enhance the smartphone experience beyond the photo enhancement that has been one of the leading manifestations to date. Indeed, they began with the original cell phone application: Voice calls. By using AI to identify the voice of the speaker, a phone would be able to virtually eliminate any background noise from a call, be it some reserved office chatter or raucous city street noise. This capability extended far beyond that of even today's best noise cancelling and into the realm of noise elimination.</p>, <p>Another demonstration showed the ability to improve the focus and bokeh of a photo that had already been taken or to change it after the fact in a manner pioneered by the <a href="https://www.cnet.com/news/google-may-acquire-light-field-tech-company-lytro-for-vr-ar/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">first Lytro camera</a>. A third showed the ability to change the hair color on the fly of a woman swaying against a colorful background in a 60fps video or to replace that background on the fly in a way that would require a skilled video editor using sophisticated compositing software today.</p>, <p><strong>Also:\xa0</strong><a href="https://www.zdnet.com/article/ai-startup-gyrfalcon-spins-plethora-of-chips-for-machine-learning/" target="_blank"><strong>AI Startup Gyrfalcon spins plethora of chips for machine learning</strong></a></p>, <p>But what may be even more impressive than how effective these techniques are is how efficient they are, at least when it comes to hardware. Today's noise-cancelling techniques, for example, use multiple microphones in order to capture and muffle distractions such as jet engine noise that has seeped into the cabin. In contrast, the AI-driven noise reduction demonstrated by Qualcomm needed only one microphone. Similarly, while the kind of depth-sensing that enables tasks such as background blurring typically uses multiple cameras, the demonstrations that Qualcomm gave used just one. Google, of course, is already creating some of these effects with the Pixel 3's sole rear camera. Apple is as well on the <a href="https://www.zdnet.com/product/apple-iphone-xr/" target="_blank">iPhone XR</a>, although the company claims the two-camera approach on its iPhone XS phones produces better results.</p>, <p>All these applications highlight the ability of AI to recognize and isolate different kinds of media objects and then act on them to improve an experience. While the photo and video capabilities are far more visually compelling, the conversation noise elimination one represents the kind of utility that stands to dramatically improve smartphone usage scenarios for a broad base of users in a transformative way.</p>, <p><strong>Also:\xa0</strong><a href="https://www.zdnet.com/article/ai-startup-cornami-reveals-details-of-neural-net-chip/" target="_blank"><strong>AI Startup Cornami reveals details of neural net chip</strong></a></p>, <p>Of course, taking best advantage of them will only be possible with the latest, premium smartphone chips. And while that cost might be offset by some component savings, those components may have other applications that can't currently be addressed by the leading-edge technology. But for many cases, AI is poised not only to offer an alternative way of achieving everyday tasks, but addressing them in a way that other approaches simply can't match.</p>, <p><em>Disclaimer: This article references announcements and discussions that took place at Qualcomm's third annual Snapdragon Summit for which Qualcomm paid travel and lodging expenses.</em></p>, <p><strong><a href="https://www.zdnet.com/article/artificial-intelligence-machine-learning-momentum-continues-to-build/" target="_blank">Artificial intelligence, machine learning momentum continues to build target="_blank">South Korea to develop AI to prevent voice phishing </a><br/></strong>With voice phishing attacks increasing by 74 percent, South Korea's Financial Supervisory Service and SK Telecom will develop AI to prevent such attacks.</p>, <p><strong><a href="https://www.cnet.com/news/ai-is-very-stupid-says-google-ai-leader-compared-to-humans/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">'AI is very, very stupid,' says Google's AI leader, at least compared to humans</a><br/></strong>Be aware of the limits of artificial intelligence, not just the hype.</p>, <p class="topicName">5G</p>, And Python is ideal when programmer time matters more than CPU time.</p>, <p>That said, if a given Python app is laggy, you\u2019re not obliged to just suck it up. Tools included with the stock installation of the Python interpreter can provide you with detailed feedback about which parts of your program are slow, and offer some hints about how to speed them up.</p>, <p>The <a href="https://docs.python.org/3.7/library/profile.html#module-cProfile" rel="nofollow"><code>cProfile</code> module</a> gathers statistics about the execution time of a Python program. [<p><a href="/user/new">Register</a> - <a href="/forgot-password">Forgot Password</a></p>, <p>By creating an account, you verify that you are at least 13 years of age, and have read and agree to the Comicbook.com <a href="/page/termsofservice">Terms of Service</a> and <a href="/page/privacy">Privacy Policy</a></p>, <p class="author">\n\t\tBy <span>Liana 'LiLi' Ruppert</span>\n<time> - January 3, 2019</time>\n</p>, <p><em>Counter-Strike: Global Offensive </em>is an incredibly popular multiplayer game by Valve that has a cult following from its player base. From pro tornaments, to a high concurrent player count, <a href="//comicbook.com/category/cs-go">CS:GO</a> is a title meant to be played. When the team decided that the game should move to free-to-play status in addition to adding a battle royale mode, the community was mixed with their reactions. As it turns out, it was one of the best decisions the developers could have made. </p>, <p>Though the most recent charting of concurrent players doesn't beat out their all time high of 850,000, the December month since going free-to-play did peak at 746, 548, which was a notable increase from November's 546,031. Since the average peak last year was 300,000, the stark increase means that the move - despite controversial at first - was the right move to make.</p>, <p>When the game first moved to free-to-play status, the Steam page was review bombed almost instantaneously. When it was bombarded with over 14,000 negative reviews, many thought this could be the mark of a decline for the noteworthy game. Though we've only had a month to see past the initial change, it's good to see that the reaction to the game is back to being more level-headed versus a knee-jerk response to the big change. </p>, <p>With the new battle royale experience now available, there's a certain freshness to the game as well. According to Valve, <em>Danger Zone </em>offers a fast-paced online experience - taking on the Battle Royale genre by storm. Using the traditional mechanics and tactical gameplay that <a href="//comicbook.com/category/cs-go">CS:GO</a> is known for, <em>Danger Zone </em>challenges players to take what they know and use it in the ultimate battle for survival.</p>, <p>Here's what you need to know about the latest addition to the award-winning shooter:</p>, <p>Players will also have an arsenal available to them that are already familiar to <a href="/category/cs-go">CS:GO</a> players. From SMGs, to rifles - and of course the heavy artillery that the game is known for, this new experience may be different for the franchise but it will still have a familiar feel to it.</p>, <p>What do you think about Valve's decision to add in battle royale and go free-to-play? Join in on the conversation in the comment section below, or hit me up over on Twitter <a href="//twitter.com/DirtyEffinHippy" target="_blank">@</a><a href="//twitter.com/DirtyEffinHippy" target="_blank">DirtyEffinHippy.</a></p>, <p>[H/T <a href="//www.pcgamesn.com/counter-strike-global-offensive/csgo-player-count" target="_blank">PCGamesN</a>]</p>, <p><span class="slidenumber"></span> of <span class="slidetotal"></span></p>, <p><img src="https://www.gamespot.com/bundles/phoenixsite/images/core/loose/logo-gamespot-clear.png"/> Copyright 2018 ComicBook.com. [<p id="skip-link"> <a class="element-invisible element-focusable" href="#main-menu">Jump to navigation</a></p>, <p>WhatsApp made some major announcements in the year 2018. The company introduced an array of updates like delete button, group calls, PiP mode, Stickers and more. All of these features are important and interesting but there's more that can be done with the app.</p>, <p>For example wouldn't it be cool if WhatsApp had a feature that could inform you as soon as your best friend came online or a feature that could let others know that you are not in the mood to chat at the moment. It would be so much better then.</p>, <p>These and similar more features we have listed below that could make WhatsApp a much better app this year. Check it out:</p>, <p><strong>-- Ignore button: </strong>WhatsApp can add an ignore button that could let the other person know that he or she is being ignored. Blue ticks leave one hanging on to hope that he or she may get a reply not immediately but surely. Ignore button would end this wait by straight away letting the sender know that the recipient is not interested in his or her messages. Ouch!</p>, <p><strong>-- Auto sent messages on festivals:</strong> Another highly-desirable feature that we want on WhatsApp. Sending message to each and every family member on a festival can be a fight in itself. It would be great if WhatsApp comes up with a feature that automatically sends wishing messages to selected contacts on festivals.</p>, <p><strong>-- Like and dislike button for Status:</strong> Ever since WhatsApp brought this feature, people have cramped the given space with all kinds of photos and texts. Like and dislike button will help those who post in Status know if their posts are pleasing or annoying.</p>, <p><strong>-- Do not disturb: </strong>WhatsApp has a mute option that mutes the chat for a specific time period but it does not stop the messages from coming. The messages keep coming and show up as unread chats in your WhatsApp window. WhatsApp can have a DND mode for the app that informs all the contacts that you are unavailable for chatting and that they should not send you any messages during then.</p>, <p><strong>-- Schedule messages:</strong> Facebook has an option to schedule post so that it appears only when you want it to. A similar feature can be added to WhatsApp that allows you to schedule your messages.</p>, <p><strong>-- Profile picture viewers:</strong> WhatsApp profile pictures are no less than Facebook profile pictures. Everyone secretly wants his or her profile picture to be looked at and admired by others. WhatsApp can have a functionality that lets you know who all have viewed your profile pictures.</p>, <p><strong>-- Notification when contact comes online: </strong>There are times when you want to chat but the other person is probably busy elsewhere. This feature can come to use then. href="https://www.geek.com/category/deals-2/">More</a></p>, <p>We all know what would happen if you screamed in space (thanks, <em>Alien</em>), but what happens if you call 911 from space?</p>, <p>In a recent interview\xa0with Dutch public broadcaster <a href="https://nos.nl/artikel/2265878-andre-kuipers-belde-per-ongeluk-alarmnummer-911-vanuit-de-ruimte.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Nederlandse Omroep Stichting</a>\xa0(NOS), Dutch astronaut Andr\xe9 Kuipers described accidentally dialing the emergency services number while in orbit aboard the International Space Station.</p>, <p>Kuipers, an astronaut with the European Space Agency, missed dialing an essential number when making a call via Houston, and ended up connecting with the U.S. emergency switchboard.</p>, <p>\u201cIf you\u2019re in space, it\u2019s like you\u2019re making a call via Houston, first you dial the 9 for an outside line, and then 011 for an international line,\u201d Kuipers told NOS.</p>, <p>The call set off\xa0a security alert at NASA\u2019s Johnson Space Center in Houston and a security team rushed to check the room through which his call had connected.</p>, <p>The team, of course, found nothing wrong. \u201cI made a mistake,\u201d Kuipers said. \u201cThe next day I received an email message: did you call 911?\u201d</p>, <p>Kuipers joked that he felt let down that nobody had arrived in response to his call. \u201cI was a little disappointed that they had not come up,\u201d he said.</p>, <p>The 60-year-old space traveler spent nine days on the ISS, conducting 21 experiments in the fields of human physiology, biology, microbiology, physical science, Earth observation, education and technology. He was the seventh European astronaut to visit the ISS, and the first from the Netherlands.</p>, <p>Long-distance calls are available to crew members of the ISS.</p>, <p>In a <a href="https://www.spaceanswers.com/space-exploration/can-astronauts-phone-home-whenever-they-want/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">2013 interview with Space Answers</a>, NASA Flight Director Holly Riddings said astronauts in the ISS use an IP phone, which works functionally through a computer. \u201cIt\u2019s kind of like \u2018Space Skype\u2019. They can call any phone in the world if they have the right satellite coverage,\u201d she said.</p>, <p>It seems astronauts calling the wrong number could be a thing. In 2015, British astronaut <a href="https://twitter.com/astro_timpeake/status/680162260946423808?lang=en" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Tim Peake tweeted</a>\xa0an apology to a woman he accidentally called. He said: \u201cI\u2019d like to apologise to the lady I just called by mistake saying \u2018Hello, is this planet Earth?\u2019 \u2013 not a prank call\u2026just a wrong number!\u201d</p>, <p>Italian astronaut Samantha Cristoforetti then <a href="https://twitter.com/AstroSamantha/status/680342998366945280" rel="noopener" target="_blank">responded to Peake\u2019s tweet</a>: \u201cHa, ha! I called 911 once by mistake.\u201d</p>, <p><em><strong>More on Geek.com:</strong></em></p>, <p>\n<a href="https://www.geek.com/category/news/">More</a>\n</p>, <p>\n<a href="https://www.geek.com/page/2/">More</a>\n</p>, <p>\n            \xa9 1996-2019            <a href="http://www.ziffdavis.com/" target="_blank">Ziff Davis, LLC. [<p class=""></p>, <p class=""> In just a few decades, <a href="https://www.thisisinsider.com/category/technology">technology</a> has gone from Walkmans that play cassette tapes to <a href="https://www.thisisinsider.com/category/iphone">iPhones</a> that play music and videos, make calls, connect to the internet, take photos, and perform countless other tasks. </p>, <p class=""> The <a href="https://www.thisisinsider.com/25-everyday-things-made-obsolete-this-century-2016-6"> swift pace of progress</a> means that some gadgets get left behind. </p>, <p class=""> Here are 16 pieces of technology from the last 50 years that are no longer in use. </p>, <p class=""> This original portable music player was popular during the 1980s. The first model sold only 3,000 units in its first month of release in <a href="https://www.history.com/this-day-in-history/the-first-sony-walkman-goes-on-sale"> 1979</a>. Clever marketing on the streets of Tokyo saved the personal cassette player, and sales soared the very next month. <a href="https://techcrunch.com/2010/10/22/an-era-ends-sony-stops-manufacturing-cassette-walkmans/">Sony stopped producing new Walkmans in 2010</a> after a successful 30-year run. </p>, <p class=""> Emergency services still use pagers since they're more <a href="https://motherboard.vice.com/en_us/article/xyw9zq/why-are-pagers-still-a-thing"> reliable than cell phones during natural disasters,</a> but they've otherwise vanished from popular use. </p>, <p class=""> The Motorola RAZR was released in 2004 and became the <a href="https://www.digitaltrends.com/mobile/ghosts-of-christmas-past-the-original-motorola-razr/"> best-selling flip phone of all time</a> with over 130 million sold over four years. The iPhone made it pretty obsolete \u2014 a 2008 report found that <a href="https://www.cnet.com/news/study-gives-insight-into-iphone-users/"> 23.8% of iPhone users</a> had switched over from the RAZR. </p>, <p class=""> The original <a href="http://www.computinghistory.org.uk/det/4033/Nintendo-Game-Boy/">Nintendo Game Boy was released in 1989</a>. The small monochrome screen and modest onboard power didn't stop this predecessor of the Nintendo 3Ds from <a href="https://www.fool.com/investing/general/2014/04/30/nintendos-game-boy-turns-25-a-look-back-at-the-bus.aspx">outselling</a> its better equipped competitors. The model was <a href="https://www.theguardian.com/technology/2014/apr/21/nintendo-game-boy-25-facts-for-its-25th-anniversary">discontinued</a> in the early 2000s. </p>, <p class=""> The <a href="https://www.format.com/magazine/features/design/you-have-died-of-dysentery-oregon-trail-design">1985 Apple II version of "The Oregon Trail"</a> is considered the original by many who have played it. But the true original version of the game was <a href="http://mentalfloss.com/article/523694/sally-died-dysentery-history-oregon-trail">released in 1971</a> for Teletype machines. Production of the popular video game ended years ago, but the gameplay lives on in a <a href="https://arstechnica.com/gaming/2016/09/oregon-trail-card-game-simple-repetitive-and-youll-die-of-dysentery-a-lot/">new tabletop card game</a> and online at the <a href="https://archive.org/details/msdos_Oregon_Trail_The_1990">Internet Archive</a>. </p>, <p class=""> Panasonic produced the <a href="https://www.panasonic.com/global/corporate/history/chronicle/1998.html"> first portable DVD players</a> in 1998. Now most laptops <a href="https://www.lifewire.com/death-of-the-computer-optical-drive-832403"> don't even come with a CD drive</a>. </p>, <p class=""> The first commercial provider of dial-up internet access <a href="https://www.livescience.com/20727-internet-history.html">launched in 1989</a>. Children of the '90s will remember that characteristic beeping sound as the internet connection was made and tying up phone lines while browsing the web. </p>, <p class=""> A 2013 Pew Research Center study found that just <a href="http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2013/08/21/3-of-americans-use-dial-up-at-home/"> three percent of Americans still use dial-up at home</a>. </p>, <p class=""> American inventor Christopher Latham Sholes <a href="https://www.britannica.com/technology/typewriter">was inspired to build the first typewriter in 1867</a>, with the machine finally hitting the market in 1874. Though computers have overwhelmingly replaced this archaic form of producing typed content, typewriters still have their fans today, <a href="https://www.vice.com/en_us/article/yvqa3y/people-are-still-using-typewriters-you-just-stopped-paying-attention-313"> among them, reportedly, Tom Hanks</a>. </p>, <p class=""> Palm Computing's first digital assistant, the Pilot 1000, <a href="https://www.pcworld.com/article/167231/history_of_palm.html#slide2"> hit the market in 1996.</a> While PDAs were able to hold <a href="https://www.zdnet.com/article/you-can-buy-a-new-iphone-for-less-than-the-original-palmpilot/"> address books, appointments, and notes</a>, they were overtaken by iPhones and Androids, which featured far more advanced capabilities, within 20 years. </p>, <p class=""> The first digital camera was <a href="https://petapixel.com/2010/08/05/the-worlds-first-digital-camera-by-kodak-and-steve-sasson/"> created in 1975 by</a><a href="https://petapixel.com/2010/08/05/the-worlds-first-digital-camera-by-kodak-and-steve-sasson/"> Steve Sasson</a>. It weighed eight pounds and took 23 seconds to create a photo. </p>, <p class=""> As the technology improved and brought pocket-sized, battery-operated cameras to the scene, sales rose in the early 2000s. But as smartphone cameras became the norm, <a href="https://www.businessinsider.com/digital-camera-shipments-15-years-decline-and-rise-2018-2"> sales steadily declined starting in 2011</a>, rising only slightly in 2017. </p>, <p class=""> AT&amp;T <a href="http://articles.latimes.com/2009/nov/22/business/la-fi-lazarus22-2009nov22">announced</a><a href="http://articles.latimes.com/2009/nov/22/business/la-fi-lazarus22-2009nov22"> that it was leaving the pay phone market</a> back in 2007, another public gadget made unnecessary thanks to cell phones. </p>, <p class=""> PC World <a href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/finance/2803487/PC-World-announces-the-end-of-the-floppy-disk.html"> announced that they would stop selling floppy disks</a> in 2007. External hard drives, thumb drives, or "the cloud" are now the way to go. </p>, <p class=""> 2016 was the first year that a majority of American homes did not have a landline, according to the <a href="https://www.cdc.gov/nchs/data/nhis/earlyrelease/wireless201705.pdf">Center for Disease Control</a>, and more than 70% of all adults aged 25 to 34 were living in wireless-only households. Home phone numbers are on their way out. </p>, <p class=""> A 2012 Pew Research Center study found that <a href="http://www.pewinternet.org/2012/03/19/what-teens-do-with-their-phones/"> 25% of teens don't ever talk on a cell phone</a>. These days, texting is easier and less awkward than recording a voicemail. Some smartphones even transcribe voicemail messages automatically, rendering answering machines a thing of the past. </p>, <p class=""> Kodachrome film was <a href="https://finance.yahoo.com/news/kodak-stopped-making-film-nearly-190829563.html"> discontinued in 2010</a>, but Kodak recently announced it would start producing another kind of film that can be processed more quickly called Ektachrome. Thanks to digital smartphone cameras or DSLRs, people rarely have film developed these days. </p>, <p class=""> In 1987, <a href="https://www.forbes.com/sites/brittanyhodak/2016/07/23/rip-vhs-worlds-last-vcr-to-be-made-this-month/#70eb10a23da1"> 90% of the $5.25 billion VCR market in the US</a> was based on the VHS format, according to Forbes. DVD players <a href="http://www.telegraph.co.uk/technology/3335984/DVD-kills-the-video-show-as-digital-age-takes-over.html"> first</a> outsold VCRs in 2002. By 2004, they were outselling them at <a href="http://www.telegraph.co.uk/technology/3335984/DVD-kills-the-video-show-as-digital-age-takes-over.html"> 40 to 1</a>. The last VCRs were <a href="https://www.forbes.com/sites/brittanyhodak/2016/07/23/rip-vhs-worlds-last-vcr-to-be-made-this-month/#70eb10a23da1"> produced in 2008</a>. </p>, <p class=""> CDs outsold cassette tapes in 1991 and peaked in the late '90s, but <a href="https://www.thisisinsider.com/the-compact-disc-industry-is-officially-dead-charts-2018-2"> sales have been declining every year since 2006</a> as music streaming platforms become the norm. Best Buy <a href="https://www.businessinsider.com/why-best-buy-is-pulling-cds-from-stores-photos-2018-2"> pulled most CDs from its stores</a> in July 2018. </p>, <p class=""><em class="">Visit </em><a href="https://www.thisisinsider.com/"><em class="">INSIDER's homepage</em></a><em class=""> for more.</em></p>, <p class=""> Like what you see here? Subscribe to our daily newsletter to get more of it. </p>, <p class=""><a href="http://e.businessinsider.com/join/insider-social-first" target="_blank">Sign-Up</a></p>]
