[<p>It\u2019s not easy to just cozy up to a rock barely longer than the Empire State Building.</p>, <p>Artist's concept of OSIRIS-REx entering orbit at asteroid Bennu.</p>, <p>Heather Roper/University of Arizona</p>, <p>While <a href="https://www.popsci.com/nasa-images-new-horizons-flyby-mu69">New Horizons soaked up most of the world\u2019s thirst for space stories</a> over the holiday, there was another success story worth unpacking: <a href="https://www.popsci.com/megapixels-nasa-asteroid-bennu">NASA\u2019s OSIRIS-REx spacecraft</a> finally <a href="https://solarsystem.nasa.gov/news/805/nasas-osiris-rex-spacecraft-enters-close-orbit-around-bennu-breaking-record/">entered asteroid Bennu\u2019s orbit</a>, after <a href="https://www.popsci.com/nasa-asteroid-mission-osiris-rex-launch">more than two years of hurtling through space</a> toward the rock. On the afternoon of December 31, about 70 million miles away from Earth, Bennu broke the record for becoming the smallest object in space to have a human-made spacecraft in its orbit.</p>, <p>This was not a routine operation for NASA. Trying to insert a spacecraft into the orbit of an object like Bennu is a fraught process. The team at NASA ended up having to account for a myriad of variables that could have derailed the entire thing.</p>, <p><a href="https://www.popsci.com/tags/osiris-rex">OSIRIS-REx</a> currently sits in an elliptical orbit about a mile from the center of Bennu, taking 61 hours to complete a full spin. Bennu itself has a diameter of about 0.3 miles, and a mass of about 78 billion kilograms. The bigger the mass, the bigger the gravity\u2014which allows for smaller objects to find their way into a stable orbit around larger objects. Unfortunately for Bennu, its small mass means it possesses 0.000005 times the gravity of Earth, which means it\u2019s relatively easy for any object to simply escape the gravitational field and just keep floating on by into space (or crash into Bennu itself if it\u2019s moving too fast). Yikes.</p>, <p>\u201c[Bennu] is nearing the smallest object that you could possibly get to achieve a stable orbit around a body,\u201d says Jason Leonard, the lead for the orbit determination team for the OSIRIS-REx mission. \u201c[Bennu\u2019s] size played the largest obstacle.\u201d But the asteroid\u2019s size is also why they chose it\u2014because some type of orbit was actually achievable. \u201cAnything else could have allowed the spacecraft to escape [orbit].\u201d</p>, <p>The small size and gravity can often become exacerbated when they interact with other forces at play. For example, the OSIRIS-REx team originally wanted to see if a circular orbit was possible, but as Leonard explains, the team soon realized that pressure created by sunlight combined with the tenuous gravity of Bennu could be enough to start pushing the spacecraft out, creating wobbles and strains in its orbit.</p>, <p>\u201cThere were early challenges, before we really knew what Bennu\u2019s shape was, what its mass was, and how it moved, that made for a lot of projected orbits that would wander back and forth,\u201d he says. The team actually didn\u2019t know what Bennu\u2019s mass or gravity field looked like until OSIRIS-REx finally arrived at the asteroid in early December. None of these unknowns created a grave concern that OSIRIS-REx would abruptly fall out of orbit or get slung out into space, but obviously, you can\u2019t really move forward with stable scientific work if you don\u2019t have a stable orbit.</p>, <p>The team\u2019s response was to ensure a \u201cfrozen orbit, which kind of takes other perturbing forces into account to help anchor the orbit [of OSIRIS-REx], so none of these other constraints impact it,\u201d says Leonard. Artificial satellites above the Earth often have frozen orbits to minimize the impact of solar pressure, gravity, and spacecraft movement on orbital drift.</p>, <p>Moving forward, the orbit determination team is keeping a keen eye on any influences caused by gravitational forces, mass redistribution on the asteroid, thermal pressures, thruster firings, solar pressure, and other physical factors that could affect how the spacecraft moves around the asteroid. In June, the team will move OSIRIS-REx into a nearer orbit, closer to half-a-mile from the surface.</p>, <p>If something unexpected does happen\u2014which would more likely be an unforeseen problem with the spacecraft\u2019s hardware or software, or an anomaly picked up by the onboard sensors\u2014the team has a built-in safety maneuver to have OSIRIS-REx escape Bennu\u2019s orbit and head toward the sun until the problem can be resolved.</p>, <p>\u201cEverything has gone incredibly well to date,\u201d says Leonard. \u201cComing in, we had a lot of contingency plans. We were planning for every single possible thing we could think of. None of that came to fruition.\u201d The mass of Bennu was less than predicted, but that had a minimal effect on the orbital insertion plan. \u201cThe spacecraft is performing much better than we ever anticipated.\u201d</p>, <p>Many of the techniques designed to pull off an orbital insertion on a small object like Bennu have only arisen in the last decade or so. Some are actually refined based on experience others have had with missions like the <a href="https://www.popsci.com/rosettas-best-moments">European Space Agency\u2019s Rosetta</a>, or <a href="https://www.popsci.com/Hayabusa-mascot-asteroid-rover">Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency\u2019s Hayabusa 1 and 2</a>. Probably the biggest lessons were taken from NASA\u2019s Near Earth Asteroid Rendezvous-Shoemaker mission from the late \u201890s and early \u201800s, which studied the near-Earth asteroid Eros.</p>, <p>The key difference is that those missions \u201cjust didn\u2019t require the precision required to get down to the surface of this small-sized asteroid,\u201d says Leonard. After all, one of the most crucial pieces of the <a href="https://www.popsci.com/what-will-happen-to-osiris-rexs-asteroid-sample">OSIRIS-REx mission is to collect an asteroid sample</a> that can go back to Earth for laboratory study.</p>, <p>There\u2019s a lot in store for OSIRIS-REx and Bennu, and the excitement is only set to build as thing unfold. \u201cThe last few months since Bennu first showed up in our cameras as a dot or speck of light, to now as a whole world teaming with boulders and features, have really brought out the enthusiasm of the team,\u201d says Leonard. \u201cWe are at the crossroads of engineering and science in deep space exploration.\u201d</p>, <p>Sign up to receive our weekly email newsletter and never miss an update!</p>, <p class="legal-text">By submitting above, you agree to <br/><a href="/privacy-policy">our privacy policy</a>.</p>, <p>You can appeal when your social media content gets taken down, but you need to know where to look.</p>, <p>It\u2019s not easy to just cozy up to a rock barely longer than the Empire State Building.</p>, <p>This robot cleaner can follow a 'smart map' of your place.</p>, <p>A Raspberry Pi 3B+ and 10 hours of instruction for $139.99.</p>, <p>A balanced diet is best, but these additions could help.</p>, <p>The secret to a healthier diet is simpler than you might think.</p>, <p>It's the first time a working rover has touched down on the far side.</p>, <p>New high-res images from New Horizons reveal a very blobby space rock.</p>, <p>Sign up to receive our email newsletter and never miss an update!</p>, <p class="legal-text">By submitting above, you agree to <a href="/privacy-policy">our privacy policy</a>.</p>, <p>Many products featured on this site were editorially chosen. [<p><span style="font-weight: 400;"><a href="https://www.thegamer.com/tag/valve/">Valve\u2019s </a>return to the world of video game development has not exactly been as triumphant as the company may have hoped, as its most recent release, </span><a href="https://www.thegamer.com/tag/artifact/"><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Artifact</span></i></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, has already seen a significant drop in Steam users playing the game.</span></p>, <p><span style="font-weight: 400;">According to </span><a href="https://www.githyp.com/valves-artifact-ended-2018-outside-steams-top-100-most-played-games/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><span style="font-weight: 400;">GitHyp</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, as of the end of 2018, </span><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Artifact</span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;"> has dropped down to only a few thousand concurrent players, after having had around 60k concurrent players when the game was released just over a month ago.</span></p>, <p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The game reached its peak as the number four most-played game on Steam during its November 28, 2018 launch, but has since fallen out of the top-100.</span></p>, <p><span style="font-weight: 400;">While the major drop comes only a month after the game\u2019s release, it really isn\u2019t much of a surprise.</span></p>, <p><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Artifact</span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;"> - Valve\u2019s first major video game release in roughly five years - has been fighting an uphill battle ever since it was </span><a href="https://www.thegamer.com/crowd-boos-valve-artifact-dota-card-game/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">announced </span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">at the International <a href="https://www.thegamer.com/tag/dota-2/"><em>DOTA 2</em></a> Championships in 2017. The digital trading card game based on </span><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">DOTA 2</span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;"> has also received backlash stemming from card controversies, such as certain card </span><a href="https://www.thegamer.com/artifact-changes-crack-whip-card-affecting-black-heroes/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">naming conventions</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></p>, <p><span style="font-weight: 400;">However, the majority of complaints are against </span><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Artifact</span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;">\u2019s monetization system. The game is available for a reasonable $19.99 USD, but anyone looking to create a competitive deck will need to shell out a considerable amount of real-life money. In fact, some of the cards have </span><a href="https://www.thegamer.com/artifacts-most-expensive-card-costs-same-price-game/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">cost as nearly as much as the game itself</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></p>, <p><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Artifact\u2019s </span></i><a href="https://www.metacritic.com/game/pc/artifact" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Metacritic score</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> has held tight at 77 since its release. However, based on its User Score of 2.1 and its massive drop in players, it is clear that it is not the Valve title that gamers were hoping for. </span></p>, <p><span style="font-weight: 400;">While </span><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Artifact </span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;">is a disappointing re-entry into the realm of game development, it shouldn\u2019t deter Valve from moving forward with other titles. Last year, Valve </span><a href="https://www.thegamer.com/campo-santo-firewatch-valley-gods-developer-valve/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">acquired </span></a><a href="https://www.thegamer.com/tag/firewatch/"><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Firewatch </span></i></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">developer Campo Santo, permitting the studio to move forward with the release of </span><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">In The Valley of Gods</span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;"> as a Valve title. And of course, rumors continue to run rampant as fans hope for a new </span><a href="https://www.thegamer.com/tag/half-life/"><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Half-Life </span></i></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">or </span><a href="https://www.thegamer.com/valve-says-its-in-a-place-to-work-on-games-again-left-3-dead-confirmed/"><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Left 4 Dead</span></i></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> game. Hopefully, </span><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">Artifact </span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;">will simply be used as Valve\u2019s blueprint for what not to do with future games.</span></p>, <p><strong class="punchline-large">READ NEXT:\xa0<a href="https://www.thegamer.com/ninja-fortnite-twitch-streamer-10-million-2018/">Ninja Earned $10 Million In 2018</a></strong></p>, <p class="article-tags">\n<strong>Tags:</strong>\n<a href="/tag/valve/">Valve</a>,\n<a href="/tag/artifact/">Artifact</a>\n</p>]
[<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Astronauts aboard the International Space Station (ISS) rely on the thin hull of the station to protect them from the vacuum of space. Even a small breach could spell disaster for the station and its crew, so personnel on the ground carefully monitor conditions. It\u2019s a good thing, too. The crew was alerted to a drop in pressure in September last year, leading to the discovery of a small hole in a Russian Soyuz capsule docked at the station. This has been the subject of much speculation, but former ISS commander Alexander Gerst now says he believes the hole was caused by a <a href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/science/2019/01/01/leak-international-space-station-blamed-botched-repair-job/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">botched repair job</a>. </span></p>, <p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The subsequent investigation of the Soyuz damage has been a roller coaster ride showcasing the declining relations between the US and Russia. Initially, NASA believed the hole was the result of a micrometeoroid impact. However, closer inspection showed several gouges and scratches that could have been made by a drill.\xa0</span><span style="font-weight: 400;">Since the damage was inside the Russian spacecraft, Roscosmos was tasked with the investigation. Russian news sources and officials have repeatedly speculated that the hole was the result of <a href="https://www.extremetech.com/extreme/276551-russian-investigators-suggest-iss-damage-could-have-been-sabotage">deliberate sabotage</a>, even going so far as to cast aspersions on the crew of the ISS. </span></p>, <p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The Soyuz capsule in question flew to the ISS in June 2018 carrying three passengers: Russia\u2019s Sergey Prokopyev, Germany\u2019s Alexander Gerst, and Serena Au\xf1\xf3n-Chancellor of the US. Gerst returned to Earth last month, and he recently sat down for an interview with BBC Radio 4. When asked about the hole, he had a much less sensational take. He believes someone on the ground damaged the spacecraft and improperly repaired it.</span></p>, <p><a href="https://www.extremetech.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/iss057e106179.jpg"><img alt="" class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-283050" height="360" sizes="(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px" src="https://www.extremetech.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/iss057e106179-640x360.jpg" srcset="https://www.extremetech.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/iss057e106179-640x360.jpg 640w, https://www.extremetech.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/iss057e106179-300x169.jpg 300w, https://www.extremetech.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/iss057e106179-223x126.jpg 223w, https://www.extremetech.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/iss057e106179-106x59.jpg 106w, https://www.extremetech.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/iss057e106179-348x196.jpg 348w, https://www.extremetech.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/iss057e106179.jpg 737w" width="640"/></a></p>, <p><span style="font-weight: 400;">According to Gerst, the hole was most likely caused by a drill, and not the kind of drill astronauts have aboard the ISS. The 2-millimeter hole in the capsule caused a drop in station pressure, but it was never life-threatening to the crew. The hole had a small spot of glue over the top, indicating someone tried to repair the damage, Gerst said. If the patch had failed while the capsule was heading to the ISS, the crew could have been in greater danger due to the smaller volume of the Soyuz compared with the whole ISS. </span></p>, <p><span style="font-weight: 400;">So, the question remains: who made the hole? There\u2019s at least one similar instance of drill damage to a Soyuz capsule. In that case, a worker on the ground damaged the spacecraft and attempted to cover up the mistake with an epoxy patch. The damage was detected pre-launch, though. Odds are something similar happened this time, but no one noticed the damage in time. It\u2019s not as sexy as an <a href="https://www.extremetech.com/extreme/276998-russian-media-spreading-absurd-conspiracy-theory-regarding-iss-damage">outer space conspiracy</a>, but few things are.</span></p>, <p>Now read:</p>, <p>Subscribe Today to get the latest ExtremeTech news delivered right to your inbox.</p>, <p>\r\n            \xa9 1996-2019            <a href="http://www.ziffdavis.com/" target="_blank">Ziff Davis, LLC. [<p>The fight over who owns the rights to the classic sci-fi role-playing strategy game \u201cStar Control\u201d continues to be messy.</p>, <p>Just recently, \u201cStar Control: Origins\u201d developer Stardock issued a statement that the game had been taken down from digital distribution platforms Steam and GOG.</p>, <p>Both platforms dropped the game from their catalogs after receiving a <a href="https://content.screencast.com/users/draginol/folders/Snagit/media/530875f0-933f-4aff-943c-d15035d58a3a/12.31.2018-16.33.png" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">Digital Millennium Copyright Act notice</a> from Paul Reiche and Fred Ford, creators of \u201cStar Control\u201d and its sequel.</p>, <p>Stardock previously attempted to get a preliminary injunction against the \u201cStar Control\u201d creators last year as a preemptive measure but was <a href="http://wiki.uqm.stack.nl/images/f/fa/102_Order.pdf" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">denied</a>.</p>, <p>It should be noted that this wasn\u2019t the first game that has been pulled from a distribution platform over a DMCA takedown request.</p>, <p>Back in 2016, open-world shooter \u201cOrion\u201d was taken down from Steam by Activision due to the game <a href="https://www.polygon.com/2016/6/27/12047914/activision-dmca-orion-pulled-from-steam-call-of-duty-trek-industries" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">allegedly using assets</a> from the game \u201cCall of Duty: Black Ops III\u201d.</p>, <p>Brad Wardell, Stardock CEO, assures that those who have already bought \u201cOrigins\u201d can still continue to play the game.</p>, <p>He also said that Stardock may have to lay off some of its employees due to the takedown.</p>, <p>Reiche, Ford and Stardock have been <a href="https://arstechnica.com/tech-policy/2018/02/star-control-countersuit-aims-to-invalidate-stardocks-trademarks/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">butting heads about \u201cStar Control\u201d</a> for more than a year now.</p>, <p>Stardock <em>claims</em> they acquired the rights to use the trademark \u201cStar Control,\u201d its assets and \u201cStar Control III\u201d after they bought it off from Atari in 2013 during the latter\u2019s bankruptcy filing sell-off.</p>, <p>Reiche and Ford, on the other hand, claim they hold the copyrights for\xa0the first two \u201cStar Control\u201d games.</p>, <p>During the development of Stardock\u2019s \u201cStar Control\u201d reboot\xa0in 2017, Reiche and Ford announced \u201cGhost of the Precursors,\u201d a direct sequel to \u201cStar Control II.\u201d</p>, <p>Few months later, the legal battle for \u201cStar Control\u201d began with Stardock filing a lawsuit against Reiche and Ford.</p>, <p>Released back in 1990, \u201cStar Control\u201d had a good reception from critics and it even\xa0gained a dedicated following.</p>, <p>It wasn\u2019t until the release of \u201cStar Control II\u201d that the series took off, garnering praise from various gaming magazines and is dubbed one of the best PC games of all time to this day.</p>, <p> <span class="figure image" itemprop="image" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject"> [<p class=""></p>, <p class=""> The break is over, and we're heading full speed into a new year that's jam-packed with major video games. </p>, <p class=""> In January alone, two massive games are scheduled to arrive: "Kingdom Hearts 3" and "Resident Evil 2." The former is a highly-anticipated sequel starring a massive list of Disney all-stars, and the latter is a highly-anticipated remake of a beloved gaming classic. </p>, <p class=""> And that's before we start talking about risky new blockbusters like "Anthem," from the folks behind "Mass Effect," and the first-ever "Mario Kart" game for smartphones! </p>, <p class=""><strong class="">Here's what to expect from the world of video games across the next three months:</strong></p>, <p class=""> The long-awaited remake of fan-favorite horror classic "Resident Evil 2" is nearly ready \u2014 it's set to arrive early in 2019, just like so many other great games currently in development. </p>, <p class=""> "Resident Evil 2" introduced the world to Leon S. Kennedy (seen above) \u2014 the main character in "Resident Evil 4." Kennedy and Claire Redfield find themselves in the middle of a surprise zombie outbreak in the fictional town of Raccoon City. It's an action-packed introduction to many of the major themes of the "Resident Evil" franchise, and it's getting gorgeously remade for modern consoles. </p>, <p class=""><strong class="">Release Date:</strong> January 25, 2019 </p>, <p class=""><strong class="">Platforms:</strong> Xbox One, PlayStation 4, PC </p>, <p class=""> Woody, Buzz, Rex and the rest of the "Toy Story" gang are moving from film to video games with "Kingdom Hearts 3," an upcoming Xbox One and PlayStation 4 action-adventure game. </p>, <p class=""> The game is the long-anticipated third entry in the "Kingdom Hearts" series \u2014 the last major entry, "Kingdom Hearts 2," launched all the way back in 2005 on the PlayStation 2. In "Kingdom Hearts," various Disney characters and their worlds are mashed up with characters that would be right at home in a "Final Fantasy" game. </p>, <p class=""> Alongside the cast of "Toy Story" (and their Earth-like setting), "Kingdom Hearts 3" also stars Goofy and Donald Duck. You may have noticed a third character here \u2014 that's "Sora," the main character of "Kingdom Hearts 3" and the one you'll play as. </p>, <p class=""><strong class="">Release Date:</strong> January 29, 2019 </p>, <p class=""><strong class="">Platforms:</strong> PlayStation 4, Xbox One </p>, <p class=""> A new "Far Cry" game? Didn't one of those come out, like, in 2018? </p>, <p class=""> Yep! That game was "Far Cry 5," and it came out back in late March on PlayStation 4, Xbox One, and PC. The open-world first-person shooter was set in America for the first time ever, and featured a new antagonist: a maniacal cult leader with nuclear ambitions. </p>, <p class=""> "Far Cry New Dawn" is a sequel to that game, set in a post-apocalypse Montana 17 years after the events of "Far Cry 5." The trailer alludes to a period of extreme weather following a nuclear detonation, eventually leading to a new world \u2014 a world where people shoot saw blades from crossbows, apparently. </p>, <p class=""><strong class="">Release Date:</strong> February 15, 2019 </p>, <p class=""><strong class="">Platforms:</strong> Xbox One, PlayStation 4, PC </p>, <p class=""> The fighting game renaissance is in full swing, and "Dead or Alive" is the next major fighting series to get a new entry in 2019. "Dead or Alive 6" continues in the tradition of the dozens of "Dead or Alive" games before it, featuring 3D fighting focused on counters and parries. </p>, <p class=""> If history is any indication, "Dead or Alive 6" will also feature stages with multiple areas and interactive elements. We'll see soon enough, as the game is due out in just a couple months. </p>, <p class=""><strong class="">Release Date:</strong> February 15, 2019 </p>, <p class=""><strong class="">Platforms:</strong> Xbox One, PlayStation 4, PC </p>, <p class=""> "Crackdown 3" has been in the works for years at this point, having been delayed multiple times. </p>, <p class=""> As the name implies, it's the third game in the open-world, third-person action "Crackdown" series. But this time, apparently, it stars Terry Crews. </p>, <p class=""> The series is big on mobility \u2014 allowing you to go anywhere you want \u2014 and huge explosions. It looks like the third game in the series is no different in this respect. </p>, <p class=""> Since "Crackdown 3" is published by Microsoft, expect it to arrive on the Xbox Game Pass service at launch \u2014 instead of buying the game for $60, you could always play it through Game Pass for far less. </p>, <p class=""><strong class="">Release Date:</strong> February 15, 2019 </p>, <p class=""><strong class="">Platforms:</strong> Xbox One, PC </p>, <p class=""> Remember "Mass Effect"? How about "Dragon Age," or "The Knights of the Old Republic"? </p>, <p class=""> That trio of blockbusters came from the folks at EA's BioWare studios \u2014 the same people behind next year's "Anthem," an all-new action-RPG. Like "Destiny," BioWare's "Anthem" is played online and focuses on players grouping up to collectively take on missions. </p>, <p class=""> Frankly speaking, what we've seen so far looks gorgeous and thrilling. Each player has the ability to fly through the air, Iron Man-style, whenever they want. It adds a layer of exploration that makes it unlike anything else available. </p>, <p class=""><strong class="">Release Date:</strong> February 22, 2019 </p>, <p class=""><strong class="">Platforms:</strong> Xbox One, PlayStation 4, PC </p>, <p class=""> Like so many other video games, the "Metro" series is set in a post-apocalyptic wasteland. Unlike many of those games, "Metro" is set in Russia. It envisions a post-apocalypse shaped by nuclear radiation, dwindling resources, and unpredictable, extreme weather conditions. </p>, <p class=""> It's a game about nuclear monsters, survival, and humanity. It's also a first-person shooter, so expect lots of shooting. </p>, <p class=""> In "Metro: Exodus," the series finally exits the underground subway tunnels of previous games for higher ground. The game is pretty straightforward: carefully pilot a dirt bike through precarious stages that are rife with traps and pitfalls. </p>, <p class=""> If you've spent any time watching bicycle or motorbike-based trials, you're no doubt familiar with what this game series is all about: Precision movement in extremely dangerous settings. "Trials" takes that formula and turns it into a risk-free video game, and then it adds massive, ridiculous explosions. </p>, <p class=""><strong class="">Release Date:</strong> February 26, 2019 </p>, <p class=""><strong class="">Platforms:</strong> Xbox One, PlayStation 4, PC, Nintendo Switch </p>, <p class=""> Early 2019 is going to be rife with slick-looking third-person action games, and "Devil May Cry 5" is the perfect example. </p>, <p class=""> The series is known for its ultra-stylish characters, deep fighting system, and over-the-top settings. [<p>The <a href="https://www.androidheadlines.com/2018/09/xiaomi-poco-f1-review-the-best-value-android-smartphone-available.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Pocophone F1</a> aka Poco F1 has managed to become quite a popular device in 2018, and even though we didn\u2019t really see any legit info regarding its successor, Ben Geskin has just <a href="https://twitter.com/VenyaGeskin1/status/1080631330034147328" rel="noopener" target="_blank">released</a> a concept render of the device. <a href="https://www.androidheadlines.com/category/xiaomi" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Xiaomi</a> is the company behind the Pocophone F1, and if this concept render ends up being close to the real design of the Pocophone F2, then you can expect a rather different approach by the company. The Pocophone F1 sported a really hard-to-miss notch, while the phone shown today comes with a tiny, waterdrop notch which houses the phone\u2019s front-facing camera, while an earpiece is placed right above it. The chin on this phone is also noticeably thinner than the one on the Pocophone F1, and the phone\u2019s display sports rounded corners. The volume up, down, and power / lock buttons are all located on the right-hand side of the phone, while the phone\u2019s SIM card tray is probably accessible from the left. A regular fingerprint scanner is shown on the back of the phone, while you will notice that there are two vertically-aligned cameras included in the top-left corner of the phone\u2019s back. A dual-LED flash is located below those two cameras, while the \u201cPoco\u201d branding is visible on the back of the phone as well. Based on the provided image, it is not exactly clear as to what materials were envisioned for this phone, but it seems like that\u2019s not glass on the back.</p>, <p><strong>Pocophone F1 vs Pocophone F2 Concept</strong></p>, <p>The Pocophone F1 did sport two cameras on the back, just like this concept Pocophone F2 smartphone, though the Pocophone F1\u2019s cameras were centered, while a fingerprint scanner was placed right below them. The curved on the back of the Pocophone F1 is also more pronounced than on this concept render, while the bezels are thinner on the Pocophone F2 render, definitely. Another obvious difference can be seen in the notch department, as the Pocophone F1\u2019s notch is quite wide, and unsightly, while the Pocophone F2 concept render comes with an Essential PH-1-like notch, which is much easier to ignore, at least for some people. This concept render really does not have to represent the upcoming Pocophone F2 smartphone, but it may, who knows, we\u2019ll just have to wait and see what is Xiaomi preparing for us.</p>, <p><strong>Pocophone F2 Arrival And What To Expect</strong></p>, <p>The Pocophone F1 managed to become so popular mainly because of its low price tag and powerful specifications. Some people consider the Pocophone F1 to be the new OnePlus One, as it not only shipped with the Snapdragon 845, 6GB / 8GB of RAM, and a large battery, but it offered a much lower price tag than the OnePlus 6 and 6T, for example. The Pocophone F1 is in a league of its own when it comes to pricing and specs ratio, and consumers will expect the same to be the case with the Pocophone F2, that\u2019s for sure. Not a single detail regarding the Pocophone F2 surfaced thus far, but it\u2019s safe to assume that it will be fueled by the Snapdragon 855 once it becomes official. The Pocophone F2 launch is quite probably far away at this point, as the Pocophone F1 arrived back in August last year, so the Pocophone F2 will probably launch in Q3 2019. The Pocophone F2 will probably include at least 6GB of RAM, while you can expect a large display to be included in the package, a display larger than 6 inches. A large battery will be a part of the offering as well, while Android 9 Pie will come pre-installed on the device, along with Xiaomi\u2019s MIUI skin with POCO customizations. The device is expected to sport two cameras on the back, and it will be interesting to see whether Poco will opt for a plastic build once again, or will it opt for metal and glass instead, which would increase the price of the phone a bit, that\u2019s for sure. The Pocophone F2 probably won\u2019t support 5G, as that would increase its price considerably, but it will include two SIM card slots, just like its predecessor, that is a given. The Pocophone F1 includes a 3.5mm headphone jack, and it will be interesting to see whether Poco will do the same with the Pocophone F2, or will it follow the trend of removing audio jacks from phones.</p>]

[<p class="clearfix">A NEW model to explain our expanding universe has been proposed by researchers that could flip our understanding of everything.</p>, <p> <img alt="Universe" class="photo kalooga_12952" data-h="414" data-w="620" src="https://cdn.images.dailystar.co.uk/dynamic/1/photos/10000/620x/Universe-751167.jpg?r=5c2dcad23488b"/><meta content="https://cdn.images.dailystar.co.uk/dynamic/1/photos/10000/620x/Universe-751167.jpg" itemprop="image"/></p>, <p>The cutting-edge cosmologists claim the universe could be riding on an expanding bubble, sitting within an extra, fourth dimension.</p>, <p>The scientists, from Sweden\u2019s Uppsala University, claimed to \u201chave devised a new model for the Universe\u201d that \u201cmay solve the enigma of dark energy,\u201d published their ideas in the Physical Review Letters.</p>, <p>They \u201cpropose a new structural concept, including dark energy, for a universe that rides on an expanding bubble in an additional dimension,\u201d the university said.</p>, <p><img alt="" class="photo kalooga_12952 swap" data-h="550" data-imgcount="1" data-media1="" data-src1="https://cdn.images.dailystar.co.uk/dynamic/1/photos/12000/1532012.jpg?r=5c2dcad23488b" data-w="620" src="https://cdn.images.dailystar.co.uk/img/static/preloaderbig.gif"/></p>, <p>For at least 20 years, a phenomenon known as \u201cblue shift\u201d has meant it is widely accepted our universe is expanding at an accelerated rate, potentially driven by a mysterious force known as dark energy.</p>, <p>The new idea relies on a theory known as the string theory, which claims all matter consists of tiny, vibrating \u201cstringlike\u201d entities.</p>, <p>String theory also requires there to be more spatial dimensions than the three - but it has not yet been able to explain dark energy in the universe.</p>, <p>However, now, \u201cthe scientists propose a new model with dark energy and our Universe riding on an expanding bubble in an extra dimension,\u201d the university says.</p>, <p><img alt="" class="photo kalooga_12952 swap" data-h="413" data-imgcount="1" data-media1="" data-src1="https://cdn.images.dailystar.co.uk/dynamic/1/photos/13000/1532013.jpg?r=5c2dcad23488b" data-w="620" src="https://cdn.images.dailystar.co.uk/img/static/preloaderbig.gif"/></p>, <p>It added: \u201cThe whole universe is accommodated on the edge of this expanding bubble.</p>, <p>"All existing matter in the universe corresponds to the ends of strings that extend out into the extra dimension.</p>, <p>\u201cThe researchers also show that expanding bubbles of this kind can come into existence within the framework of string theory.</p>, <p>\u201cIt is conceivable that there are more bubbles than ours, corresponding to other universes.\u201d</p>, <p class="lead">DECLAN Donnelly has thanked the\xa0"heroes"\xa0for taking care of one of his closest family members.</p>, <p class="lead">LIVERPOOL lost their unbeaten run at Manchester City tonight, throwing the title race wide open \u2013 and rival fans are making the same Steven Gerrard...</p>, <p class="lead">MANCHESTER City star Sergio Aguero has been spotted with a stunning mystery brunette before the star's crunch match against Liverpool.</p>, <p>Copyright \xa92019 Express Newspapers. "Daily Star" is a registered trademark. All rights reserved.</p>]

[<p class="bodytext">A recent leak <a class="internal-link" href="New-device-with-395-000-Antutu-score-is-alleged-to-be-the-Sony-Xperia-XZ4.390691.0.html" target="_self">asserts</a> that a Sony device with the model number I8134 scored just over 395,000 in Antutu Benchmark scores. Now, a new one <a class="external-link-new-window" href="https://www.gizchina.com/2019/01/03/sony-xperia-xz4-visits-geekbench-with-sd-855-8gb-ram-and-android-pie/" target="_blank">alleges</a> that the same device has gone to Geekbench 4, and scored impressively well there. On the other hand, as with the Antutu-related image, the listing as portrayed in this post is nowhere to be found on the benchmark's official website.\r</p>, <p class="bodytext">According to the latest Xperia-related <a class="external-link-new-window" href="https://www.gizchina.com/2019/01/03/sony-xperia-xz4-visits-geekbench-with-sd-855-8gb-ram-and-android-pie/" target="_blank">rumor</a>, the 'r1_I8134' scored 3497 in the single-core tests in question, and 12801 in the multi-core ones. It apparently achieved these results on January 2. They are particularly impressive, as a Sony Xperia XZ3 <a class="external-link-new-window" href="https://browser.geekbench.com/v4/cpu/11496818" target="_blank">scored</a> only 2392 and 8862 in the single- and multi-core tests respectively a day later. The former device was also listed as running Android 9.0 (Pie) and as having 8GB of RAM.\r</p>, <p class="bodytext">The purported XZ4 was <a class="external-link-new-window" href="https://www.gizchina.com/2019/01/03/sony-xperia-xz4-visits-geekbench-with-sd-855-8gb-ram-and-android-pie/" target="_blank">apparently</a> powered by a Snapdragon processor with 8 cores and a base clock of 1.78GHz. This is not a million miles away from those of the<a class="external-link-new-window" href="https://browser.geekbench.com/v4/cpu/11496818" target="_blank"> Snapdragon 845</a>; therefore, the chipset could be its successor, the 855, which <a class="external-link-new-window" href="https://www.qualcomm.com/products/snapdragon-855-mobile-platform" target="_blank">is known</a> to be an octa-core CPU that can run up to 2.84GHz. In addition, the chipset bears the code-name msmnile, which has been <a class="internal-link" href="855-no-longer-Latest-leaks-suggest-major-upheavals-for-next-SD-chipset.323550.0.html" target="_self">associated</a> with the 855 in the past. However, there is still no direct evidence that this device is the Sony Xperia XZ4, or that it even exists at this point. [<p><strong>During Overwatch Season 13, top Zarya players averaged almost 3,000 more damage per match than DPS heroes, like Soldier and Ashe did.</strong></p>, <p style="font-size:12px;color:#ccc;">Advertisement</p>, <p>DPS heroes are typically expected to have the most damage output during\xa0an Overwatch match, but it looks like the GOATs meta, which basically consists of three tanks and three healers, is giving Zarya a chance to shine.</p>, <p>GOATs became popular after an Open Division team of the same name went undefeated using the strategy for the first time. Since then, it has replaced Dive as the go-to team comp for most professional teams.</p>, <p>According to user Chief-TR on /r/Competitive Overwatch, using data taken from Overbuff, the top 10 Zarya players averaged 23,042 damage per match during Season 13.</p>, <p>This is almost 3,000 more damage per match than the top Ashe players, who averaged 20,790, or elite Hanzo mains, who averaged 20,435 damage per match.</p>, <p>Because of the way GOATs is played, Chief-TR and other users came to the conclusion that it is the prevalence of GOATs that allows Zarya to deal so much damage.</p>, <p>Some users said in the comments that it wasn\u2019t actually GOATs, but the change to close-range brawl team compositions once Brigitte was introduced into the game, that allows Zarya to gain charge and deal more damage than anyone else.</p>, <p>Since this data is only from the top 10 players for each hero, Zarya might not actually be the highest damage dealer in say, gold or platinum ranks, but when it comes to top 500, she definitely is.</p>, <p>Even though it\u2019s a small sample size, these numbers do a good job of showing the niche that Zarya has against high damage-dealing compositions, like GOATs.</p>, <p class="flex-auto ml2 my0">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tWe use cookies on this website to improve your experience. [<p><img alt="jensen huang drive nvidia ces" border="0" class="img-responsive imported-news-entry-img" height="1274" src="https://static2.businessinsider.com/image/5a53890bc32ae6df1a8b4c9f-2000/rtx46xhh.jpg" width="2000"/><span class="source">Rick Wilking/Reuters</span><!-- sh_cad_1 --></p>, <p></p>, <p>When the 2018 crypto crash rocked the cryptocurrency-mining industry, shares of the chipmakers <a href="https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/nvda-stock?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest" target="_blank">Nvidia</a> and <a href="https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/amd-stock?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest" target="_blank">AMD</a> performed wildly different.<!-- sh_cad_3 --></p>, <p><span><a href="https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/nvda-stock?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest" target="_blank">Nvidia</a></span> lost 32% last year, but <a href="https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/amd-stock?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest" target="_blank">AMD </a>gained a whopping 71%. And that's no surprise in the eyes of <span>Christopher Rolland, a s</span>emiconductor analyst at Susquehanna International Group.<!-- sh_cad_4 --></p>, <p>"Some of the differences between the two stocks are simply because Nvidia is a pure GPU player, whereas AMD has GPUs as well, they also sell a lot of CPUs," <span>Rolland told Markets Insider. </span><div class="hidden-lg hidden-md lazy" data-loader="finandoLazyLoader" id="div-Mobile-Web/Currencies/Post-2" style="text-align:center; margin:auto;"><script type="text/javascript">googletag.cmd.push(function() { googletag.display('div-Mobile-Web/Currencies/Post-2'); });</script></div><div class="hidden-xs hidden-sm adTag lazy" data-loader="finandoLazyLoader" id="div-Desktop/Currencies/Post-P5" style="text-align:center; margin:auto;"><script type="text/javascript">googletag.cmd.push(function() { googletag.display('div-Desktop/Currencies/Post-P5'); });</script></div></p>, <p><span>Simply put, a graphics processing unit (GPU) can only do a fraction of the many operations a central processing unit (CPU) does, but it does so with incredible speed. Therefore, GPUs are more cost-effective for crypto mining, but CPUs have a broader consumer base.\xa0</span><span></span><!-- sh_cad_6 --></p>, <p><span>According to Rolland, the crypto boom in 2017 led both Nvidia and AMD to overproduce GPUs for crypto mining, causing an inventory problem when digital currencies <a href="https://www.businessinsider.in/crypto-is-crashing-hard-as-bitcoin-falls-below-6000/articleshow/65398770.cms" target="_blank">crashed in 2018</a>. </span><!-- sh_cad_7 --></p>, <p><span>For AMD, thanks to its CPU business, the market has a lot more hope and optimism.\xa0</span><span>"The prospects for their CPU business versus Intel are the best that have been in decades," he said.\xa0</span><!-- sh_cad_8 --></p>, <p><span>Last year, AMD shares surged by more than 230% through the middle of September as rival <a href="https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/intc-stock?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Intel</a> was contending with a production <a href="https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/amd-stock-price-steal-market-share-intel-chip-problems-says-2018-9-1027555704?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest" target="_blank">delay for its 10-nanometer chips</a>. And while </span><span>a</span><span>\xa0research report later said <a href="https://www.businessinsider.com/intel-stock-price-report-could-speed-up-10-nanometer-chip-production-2018-10?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Intel may have cured its production problem</a> sooner than expected, analysts noted that the delay "<a href="https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/amd-stock-price-bear-market-analysts-say-buy-2018-10-1027650713?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest" target="_blank">opened the door for AMD to gain share in both servers and PCs - near and long term</a>." </span><!-- sh_cad_9 --></p>, <p><span>Also at stake is that AMD is widely expected to roll out its <a href="https://www.moodys.com/research/Moodys-upgrades-Advanced-Micro-Devices-CFR-to-Ba3-and-senior--PR_389819" target="_blank">7 nm chips</a> in the first quarter of 2019, which in theory provide better performance than 10nm ones. "There's hope that they are going to gain market share from Intel," Rolland added.</span><div class="hidden-lg hidden-md lazy" data-loader="finandoLazyLoader" id="div-Mobile-Web/Currencies/Post-3" style="text-align:center; margin:auto;"><script type="text/javascript">googletag.cmd.push(function() { googletag.display('div-Mobile-Web/Currencies/Post-3'); });</script></div></p>, <p>Another reason for the two stocks' different performance, Rolland says, could be <a href="https://markets.businessinsider.com/earnings-calendar?utm_source=markets&amp;utm_medium=ingest" target="_blank">the timing of their financial reporting</a>. Usually, Nvidia reports a month later than AMD, which means Nvidia has disclosed more information about its inventory issues.<!-- sh_cad_11 --></p>, <p>"Nvidia has already confessed fully to the amount of inventory that's out there," said Rolland. "AMD has only half confessed."<!-- sh_cad_12 --></p>, <p class="mostviewed-instruments-subheadline">Your Personalized Market Center</p>]
[<p class="description">Love cars? Climb in the driver's seat for the latest in reviews, advice and picks by our editors.</p>, <p class="sectionTitle"><strong>By</strong> Style</p>, <p class="sectionTitle"><strong>By</strong> Make &amp; Model</p>, <p><span>We cover it all,</span> click your favorite</p>, <p class="article-dek col-8">The car would reportedly pack 700 horsepower and debut by 2023.</p>, <p>Rather than directly replacing the i8, BMW may be looking to build a more expensive and more powerful hybrid supercar.</p>, <p class="speakableTextP1">We've found a lot of like about the <span class="link" section="shortcodeLink"><a href="/roadshow/reviews/2019-bmw-i8-roadster-review/">i8</a></span>, <a data-annotation="true" data-component="linkTracker" data-link-tracker-options='{"action":"inline-annotation|BMW|CNET_CMP_MFR_AUTO|643"}' href="/roadshow/make/bmw/">BMW's</a> plug-in-hybrid near-supercar. But the engineers at BMW apparently want to build something even more extreme. According to a new report from <a data-component="externalLink" href="https://www.autocar.co.uk/car-news/new-cars/bmw-plots-supercar-take-mclaren" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Autocar</a>, BMW plans to develop a new hybrid, mid-engined supercar that would compete with entries from the likes of McLaren.</p>, <p class="speakableTextP2">Autocar says that rather than a direct <span class="link" section="shortcodeLink"><a href="/roadshow/reviews/2017-bmw-i8-review/">BMW i8</a></span> successor, the new model would be much more expensive and considerably more powerful. It would reportedly use a six-cylinder engine, instead of the i8's turbocharged triple, and gutsier electric motors. All told, 700 horsepower is allegedly the target. As with the i8 -- and the supercars BMW aims to compete with -- the new model would be built from carbon fiber to keep weight low.</p>, <p>"If you are an engineer, once in your life, you want to make a super-sports car," Klaus Fr\xf6hlich, BMW's board member responsible for research and development, told Autocar. "I think partial electrification will enable that."</p>, <p>BMW has publicly committed to launching <span class="link" section="shortcodeLink"><a href="/news/bmw-readying-four-door-electric-i-concept-car-for-frankfurt-motor-show/">at least 25 electrified vehicles by 2025</a></span>, of which 13 will be fully electric. Rival supercar manufacturers are also pursing hybrid tech to improve both power and efficiency. McLaren, for instance, has said publicly that 50 percent of its lineup will be <a data-annotation="true" data-component="linkTracker" data-link-tracker-options='{"action":"inline-annotation|Hybrids|CNET_CAT_TOPIC|298"}' href="/roadshow/hybrids/">hybrids</a> by 2022 and <span class="link" section="shortcodeLink"><a href="/news/mclaren-track25-new-cars-all-hybrids/">100 percent will be hybrids by 2025</a></span>. Similarly, the <a data-annotation="true" data-component="linkTracker" data-link-tracker-options='{"action":"inline-annotation|Acura NSX|CNET_FAM_LINE_AUTO|300"}' href="/roadshow/make/acura/model/nsx/">Acura NSX</a> uses hybrid technology, and Ferrari has said its future models will use hybridization.</p>, <p>With the new hybrid supercar is not expected to debut for another four years, we've got a long time for BMW's plans to change. Still, it's an exciting reminder that a future of electrified vehicles does not mean a future devoid of powerful supercars.</p>, <p class="policy">Be respectful, keep it civil and stay on topic. [<p class="w w2" data-widget="Dateline">\nFriday 4 January 2019\n</p>, <p>\n<a href="https://www.independent.ie/opinion/independent-journalists/adrian-weckler/"><strong>Adrian Weckler</strong></a>\n<a class="icon twitter" href="https://twitter.com/@adrianweckler" target="_blank"><span>Twitter</span></a>\n<a class="icon email" href="mailto:aweckler@independent.ie"><span>Email</span></a>\n</p>, <p>\n<time>January 3 2019 2:30 AM</time>\n</p>, <p>\nGoogle may soon replace your phone screen with gesture controls you use in mid-air, like a scene from the film 'Minority Report'.\n</p>, <p>The tech giant has received the all-clear from authorities to develop a motion sensor that uses lasers to sense what your fingers are doing away from the screen.</p>, <p>The technology has been touted as a potential breakthrough for those with mobility or speech impairments. It also means that problems such as cracked screens may not be as big of an issue as they are at present.</p>, <p>Google says the sensor can allow users to press an invisible 'button' between the thumb and index fingers or a virtual dial that turns by rubbing a thumb against the index finger.</p>, <p>It means that we may soon control gadgets such as phones and smartwatches by gesturing rather than tapping the screen.</p>, <p>The company, which recently started selling smartphones and other devices directly in Ireland, has been trying to win approval for the technology for three years. Now, both European and US regulatory bodies have said that Google can build and release devices using the technology, called Project Soli, accepting it won't interfere with aeroplanes or other sensitive frequencies.</p>, <p>The company says that "even though these controls are virtual, the interactions feel physical and responsive" as feedback is generated by the haptic sensation of fingers touching.</p>, <p>It could add a further boost to gadgets with small screens, such as smart watches and fitness wearables, which have displays that are often clumsy to use with human fingers.</p>, <p>Granting Google leave to pursue the system, US regulators have said that the decision "will serve the public interest by providing for innovative device control features using touchless hand gesture technology".</p>, <p>Such technology was popularised in the movie 'Minority Report', where actors Tom Cruise and Colin Farrell used gesture controls to swipe and select virtual computer screens.</p>, <p>Google says the new tools can approximate the precision of natural human hand motion and the sensor can be embedded in wearables, phones, computers and vehicles.</p>, <p>However, the company is not yet saying when a finished product will be ready for market, nor whether it will license the technology to technology rivals such as Apple and Samsung.</p>, <p>Facebook, which had objected to the system for technical frequency reasons, now says that it accepts the technology will have a "variety of use cases" in future.</p>, <p class="originalSource">\nIrish Independent\n</p>, [<p>What if you could use information about your existing customers to obtain new ones? That\u2019s the purpose of Audience Insights in Google Ads. It helps businesses find new prospects based on current customer data.</p>, <p><a href="https://support.google.com/google-ads/answer/3726570?co=ADWORDS.IsAWNCustomer%3Dfalse&amp;hl=en">Audience Insights</a> uses data from your Google Ads\u2019 remarketing lists. Audience Insights can provide helpful details about the people on those lists.</p>, <p>For example, advertisers using conversion tracking can turn to Audience Insights to find prospects related to your \u201cAll Converters\u201d remarketing list \u2014 i.e., buyers. With the details from this report, marketers can expand their targeting or adjust ad bids to reach these high-performing audiences.</p>, <p class="p1"><span class="s1">It\u2019s important to know that the Audience Insights report does not appear by default \u2014 advertisers must activate it. And it\u2019s only available to Google Ads\u2019 advertisers with remarketing campaigns. The \u201cinsights\u201d come from an advertiser\u2019s remarketing contacts.\xa0</span></p>, <p class="p1"><span class="s1">To locate the Audience Insights report in Google Ads, go to <em>Tools &gt; Audience Manager</em>. It will be on the left side. If you aren\u2019t running Google Ads\u2019 remarketing campaigns, you\u2019re out of luck. But this might be a good reason to start.</span></p>, <p>Beyond advertising, Audience Insights can help with search engine optimization by identifying keywords to focus on.</p>, <p>Consider the screenshot below of an Audience Insights report. It provides details of consumers on a merchant\u2019s remarketing list. \u201cIn-market\u201d describes the broad industries those consumers are interested in based on their search history and other online activity. \u201cAffinity\u201d describes, roughly, the consumers\u2019 association with the in-market industry.</p>, <p class="wp-caption-text">This sample Audience Insights report provides details of consumers on a merchant\u2019s remarketing list. <em>Source: Search Engine Land.</em></p>, <p>From this high-level view, we can conclude that many of the consumers on the above remarketing list are interested in \u201cChristmas Items &amp; Decor.\u201d They are \u201cHome Decor Enthusiasts\u201d and \u201cDo-It-Yourselfers.\u201d If this were your report, and you sell holiday decorating items, you could create content on ideas for using your products via blog posts, videos, and product descriptions. All could appear in organic search results and appeal to relevant shoppers.</p>, <p>Audience Insights can also show how much more frequently your users convert by category or product when compared to the typical website user. In the example below, looking in the \u201cIndex\u201d column, note that people in the \u201cCarpet Installation\u201d audience convert 15.5 times more frequently than the average searcher.</p>, <p class="wp-caption-text">The \u201cCarpet Installation\u201d audience convert 15.5 times more frequently than the average searcher, as noted in the \u201cIndex\u201d column. <em>Click image to enlarge.\xa0</em></p>, <p>For a business that converts a large percentage of consumers searching for carpeting, it makes sense to <a href="https://www.practicalecommerce.com/the-key-requirement-of-content-marketing">spend money on content</a>, such as the benefits of buying installed carpeting rather than area rugs. It could pepper more carpet-related content into guides, blog posts,\xa0and social content.</p>, <p>However, for the same business, allocating budget to, say, a blog post about \u201cDesign Software\u201d (with a 7.6 conversion multiple) may help users, but it won\u2019t win nearly the same carpeting sales.</p>, <p class="p1"><span class="s1">Leveraging Google Ads\u2019 data for SEO campaigns can be very helpful in my experience. Unfortunately, it\u2019s common for SEO and PPC teams to work independently. I see it all the time; teams do not share data \u2014 in-house and at external agencies. </span></p>, <p class="p1"><span class="s1">Google has greatly reduced access to organic search data. But it\u2019s readily available to those who pay for Google Ads. While the Performance tab in the new <a href="https://www.practicalecommerce.com/search-console-is-the-gateway-to-google-seo-data">Google Search Console</a> contains some of this organic data, it\u2019s not to the level of Google Ads.</span></p>, <p class="p1"><span class="s1">If the silo exists in your company, fix it. If you work with an agency that does not share its data, have a serious conversation. SEO practitioners need to know what their potential audience wants. Every query entered into a search engine is a need. Understanding those needs helps to create relevant content. It\u2019s that simple.</span></p>, <p>I\u2019ve heard people say that SEO produces free traffic. True, you don\u2019t pay directly for the traffic, but it\u2019s not free. You still need to invest time and money. What better way than <a href="https://www.practicalecommerce.com/7-ways-integrate-natural-paid-search">through Google Ads</a>?</p>, <p>When you\u2019re using the \u201ctargeting\u201d setting (such as affinity audiences, placements, or remarketing) for your campaigns or ad groups, you\u2019re telling Google Ads who you\u2019d like to reach with your ads or where you\u2019d like your ads to show across the internet. Use that setting in your ad groups or campaigns to show to specific audiences or on specific content. Experiment and learn even more about your audience.</p>, <p>Here are a few ways to continue the discovery.</p>, <p>\n                        Copyright \xa9 2005 - 2019.<br/>\n                        Practical Ecommerce\xae is a <br/>\n                        registered trademark of  <br/>\n                        Confluence Distribution, Inc.  <br/></p>]

[<p>Our websites may use cookies to personalize and enhance your experience. By continuing without changing your cookie settings, you agree to this collection. For more information, please see our <a href="https://privacy.uconn.edu/university-website-notice/" target="_blank">University Websites Privacy Notice</a>.</p>, <p class="post-date-author"><span class="byline-date grey-text">January 3, 2019</span> - <span class="small-title"><a href="https://today.uconn.edu/author/bre10001/">Bret Eckhardt</a> - UConn Communications, and <a href="https://today.uconn.edu/author/ems07004/">Elaina Hancock</a> - UConn Communications</span></p>, <p class="caption-text">Reducing your greenhouse gas emissions can be as easy as changing the types of food you buy and eat, according to a recent study led by UConn researchers. (<span id="videoCredit"></span>) </p>, <p>A recent study led by researchers at UConn suggests that if Americans directed their food purchases away from meats and other animal proteins, they could help reduce greenhouse gas emissions.</p>, <p>The complex industrial supply chain that produces food generates an estimated 16 percent of U.S. greenhouse gas emissions in 2013, according to the study,\xa0<a href="http://www.uconnruddcenter.org/files/Pdfs/A%20Comprehensive%20Life%20Cycle%20Assessment%20of%20Greenhouse%20Gas%20Emissions%20from%20U_S_%20Household%20Food%20Choices.pdf">published in June in\xa0the journal\xa0<em>Food Policy</em></a>.</p>, <p>\u201cWe found that households that spend more of their weekly food budget on beef, chicken, pork, and other meats are generating more greenhouse gas emissions,\u201d says Rebecca Boehm, the study\u2019s lead author, a former postdoctoral fellow in the Department of Agricultural and Resource Economics at UConn.\xa0\u201cEncouraging consumers to make food choices that are lower in greenhouse gas emissions can make a real difference addressing climate change.\u201d These choices focus on opting for less animal protein in the form of red meat and dairy, and instead choosing proteins that are less carbon-intensive, such as seafood, poultry, and legumes.</p>, <p>The study team included researchers at the\xa0<a href="http://www.uconnruddcenter.org/">UConn Rudd Center for Food Policy and Obesity</a>;\xa0<a href="http://www.zwickcenter.uconn.edu/">UConn Zwick Center for Food and Resource Policy</a>; Tufts University Friedman School of Nutrition Science and Policy; the University of Missouri; and the U.S. Department of Agriculture\u2019s Economic Research Service. Boehm is now working as an economist for the Union of Concerned Scientists in Washington, D.C.</p>, <p data-elm-loc="4">\n<div data-id="144843" data-site-id="1841" data-tags="bre10001,ems07004,bre10001,College of Agriculture Health and Natural Resources,Copy Editors,ejo02002,ems07004,environment,jac05005,jas16118,krc13023,pae02003,Video,postdoctoral fellows,research,slp02008,video" data-title="Climate Change: It (Doesn't Have to Be) What's for Dinner" data-url="https://today.uconn.edu/2019/01/climate-change-doesnt-whats-dinner/" id="NamForm"></div>\n</p>, <p class="small-title footer-share-btns">\n<span class="grey-text">SHARE </span>\n<span class="footer-share-btn-wrap">\n<span class="twitter" data-description="Climate Change: It (Doesn\u2019t Have to Be) What\u2019s for Dinner" data-name="Climate Change: It (Doesn\u2019t Have to Be) What\u2019s for Dinner" data-picture="https://uconn-today-universityofconn.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/Climate-Change-Thumbnail-1_cropped-150x150.jpg" data-text="Climate Change: It (Doesn\u2019t Have to Be) What\u2019s for Dinner" data-url="https://today.uconn.edu/?p=144843" data-via="UConn"></span>\n<span class="facebook" data-description="Climate Change: It (Doesn\u2019t Have to Be) What\u2019s for Dinner" data-name="Climate Change: It (Doesn\u2019t Have to Be) What\u2019s for Dinner" data-picture="https://uconn-today-universityofconn.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/Climate-Change-Thumbnail-1_cropped-150x150.jpg" data-text="Climate Change: It (Doesn\u2019t Have to Be) What\u2019s for Dinner" data-url="https://today.uconn.edu/?p=144843" data-via="UConn"></span>\n<a href="mailto:?to=&amp;subject=UConn Today - [<p class="addl-text">Use commas to separate multiple email addresses</p>, <p class="msg-sent">Your message has been sent.</p>, <p class="msg-sent">There was an error emailing this page.</p>, <p class="name" itemprop="author" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">\n<a href="/author/Gregg-Keizer/" rel="author" title="Gregg Keizer"><img alt="Gregg Keizer" class="bylineImage imgId100363775 " itemprop="image" src="https://images.techhive.com/images/article/2014/07/gregg-keizer-150-100363775-byline.png" width="34"/></a>\n<span class="by">By </span><span class="fn" itemprop="name"><a href="/author/Gregg-Keizer/" itemprop="url" rel="author"><span itemprop="name">Gregg Keizer</span></a></span>\n</p>, <p class="dateline">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\tSenior Reporter, \n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n<span itemprop="publisher" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Organization"><span class="publisher" itemprop="name">Computerworld</span><meta content="https://idge.staticworld.net/ctw/computerworld-logo300x300.png" itemprop="logo"/></span> <span class="divider break">|</span>\n<span class="break-date" content="2019-01-03T12:54-0800" itemprop="datePublished">Jan 3, 2019 12:54 PM\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t PT\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</span>\n</p>, <p>Chrome users have laid into Google after the search giant scrubbed an option that let them restore an earlier user interface (UI), saying that the new look was "untenable" and "ugly," and "would burn the eyes."</p>, <p>The brouhaha, which has packed complaints into venues like Chrome's official support forum, Twitter and Reddit, grew in volume and vitriol throughout December, after Google upgraded the browser to version 71.</p>, <p>Although Google revamped Chrome's UI with version 69 - released in September to mark the browser's 10th anniversary - users were able to punt that look-and-feel for the prior by setting an option in the panel that showed after typing <i>chrome://flags</i> into the address bar. The option was labeled "UI Layout for the browser's top chrome;" switching from "Default" to "Normal" and restarting the browser restored the older UI.</p>, <p>But with Chrome 71, which Google started distributing Dec. 4, the "Normal" setting vanished.</p>, <p>That set off some users, who had been so unhappy with the even more minimalist UI, particularly the rectangular tabs and the lack of clear definition between tabs, that they'd reverted to a pre-69 design.</p>, <p>Chrome tabs in version 71.</p>, <p>"The new (tab) shape causes problems - you can't visually feel them, and the tab text gets crushed out. It's really inferior to the old shape and contrast," wrote <i>bhowes</i> in a <a href="https://productforums.google.com/forum/#!topic/chrome/Fs2z642aopE;context-place=topicsearchin/chrome/ui" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank">message</a> posted to the Chrome support forum.</p>, <p>Others chimed in. "Bring back the old GUI (graphical user interface) or I am switching," threatened <a href="https://productforums.google.com/d/msg/chrome/Fs2z642aopE/mhVM\\_1xrEAAJ" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank"><i>XeX Menu togo</i>.</a></p>, <p>"Your browser is so ugly now that it's actually unusable, and customers are leaving because of it," contended <a href="https://productforums.google.com/d/msg/chrome/Fs2z642aopE/p3R\\_YttuEAAJ" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank"><i>Ec Little</i></a>. "Whoever is responsible for this should be fired for causing Chrome to hemorrhage customers."</p>, <p>As <a href="https://www.zdnet.com/article/google-chromes-new-ui-is-ugly-and-people-are-very-angry/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank">ZDNet</a> reported a week ago, examples of similar grievances were rampant across Twitter and on Reddit. One of a slew of reddit threads spelled out a gripe in stereotypical Reddit rage. "I'm off to Firefox until Google fixes the tabs o7 I'd rather not get blinded AND vomit every time I use Chrome," wrote <a href="https://www.reddit.com/r/chrome/comments/a7fbdt/im\\_off\\_to\\_firefox\\_until\\_google\\_fixes\\_the\\_tabs\\_o7/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank"><i>ferengi4</i></a>.</p>, <p>Others just mocked the browser. "Big Brother's removed the ability to change Chrome's UI," tweeted <a href="https://twitter.com/Pancakeoflust/status/1080527051818332160" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank">Michael Schulze</a> on Wednesday. "All must embrace Fisher-Price. Press the Horse icon for any questions or complaints."</p>, <p>Here and there, some refused to bend a knee to the UI mandate and pointed others toward <a href="https://productforums.google.com/d/msg/chrome/Fs2z642aopE/\\_OvJJaYbDwAJ" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank">pre-71 copies of Chrome</a> that allowed interface roll-back.</p>, <p>A Google engineer said that would be wrong. "Please don't do this," pleaded Peter Kasting on Reddit. "As a Chrome dev, we would really rather you use another browser than try to lock yourself on an old version of Chrome. There are serious consequences to this, and much like choosing not to be vaccinated, the choice affects other people besides just you."</p>, <p>Kasting was referring to running an out-of-date version of Chrome, one that would no longer receive security updates.</p>, <p>He also downplayed Reddit-based criticism and argued that leaving a reversion option was bad practice. "Reddit posts are not an unbiased, representative sample of all feedback," he wrote. "I invite you to consider the arguments at <a href="http://neugierig.org/software/blog/2018/07/options.html" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank">(here)</a> for why teams don't necessarily choose to expose options." The link led to a post by Chrome developer Evan Martin, who argued that options were bad user experience and sometimes more trouble to maintain than a standard feature.</p>, <p>Kasting is no stranger to Chrome UI controversy. Nearly five years ago, a <a href="https://www.change.org/p/lawrence-page-replace-peter-kasting-and-the-google-chrome-ui-team" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank">petition</a> on <i>Change.org</i> demanded that Google executives fire Kasting and his UI team. "We have been betrayed by the Chrome team, having taken matters into their own hands and blatantly changing Chrome for what many see as far worse, far slower, and far less useful, but also more importantly taking away 'choice,'" said James Brown, who launched the petition.</p>, <p>Brown - and the 300 and some others who signed the online petition - were <a href="https://www.computerworld.com/article/2487910/internet/google-yanks-option-to-restore-chrome-s-old-style-new-tab-page--riles-users-all-over-again.html">upset about changes to Chrome's new tab page</a>. More than <i>upset</i>, actually; more like furious. Some of the messages left by users were definitely <a href="https://productforums.google.com/forum/#!msg/chrome/THPuNSLtljg/1EovqphG1bsJ" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank">not workplace appropriate</a> while others were creative, if leaning toward the blasphemous. "For the love of the little crying infant baby Jesus would you STOP messing with my new tab page?" asked Steve Pittman in February 2014.</p>, <p>Other crusades of UI-change complaints launched against Chrome struck out at <a href="https://www.computerworld.com/article/2487799/desktop-apps/windows-users-denounce-chrome-scrollbar-changes-that-mimic-chrome-os.html">revisions to the browser's scrollbar</a> (January 2014) and an <a href="https://www.computerworld.com/article/2913426/web-browsers/chrome-users-roast-google-on-spit-of-hate-over-revamped-bookmarks-manager.html">overhaul of its bookmark manager</a> (April 2015).</p>, <p>"HATE - HATE - HATE the new format. Again - HATE IT!!!!!!!!!" <a href="https://productforums.google.com/forum/#!msg/chrome/pAUi-WhbtjM/QLGCPaMMiakJ" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank"><i>MaryMom628</i></a> stormed over the bookmarking tool, using every last exclamation mark in her monthly allotment.</p>, <p>It's unlikely that Google will bow to user demands and return an option for the older Chrome UI; it didn't give in during any of the other donnybrooks.</p>, <p class="bio">Senior Reporter Gregg Keizer covers Windows, Office, Apple/enterprise, web browsers and web apps for Computerworld.</p>, <p><a href="/about/copyright.html">Copyright</a> \xa9 2019 IDG Communications, Inc.</p>]

Other than the fact that this person has two legs and a set of chains, our next champion has been an absolute mystery. The newest set of teaser images bring a little more clarity to the issue, although its not a full reveal yet:</p>, <p id="GijwuT">These images, entitled Visions of Demacia, suggest that this chain champion has the ability to lock down and possibly even control enemies to some degree. Lux, Galio, Garen and Jarvan IV all have their abilities or weapons on display, and those chains are clearly locking three of the above champions up to some degree.</p>, <p id="q8xden">This could be a Demacian champion who shows the nation\u2019s darker side, which has so far only been hinted at. Demacia is anti-magic to the point of fascism, and only a few rare mages \u2014 including Lux \u2014 are allowed to work and live among polite society. A champion who shows that conflict could be very interesting indeed, especially if he has magic of his own, and uses it to further Demacia\u2019s will.</p>, <p id="Nd7irX">We\u2019ll likely see more info about this upcoming champion as January progresses.</p>]
[<p class="entry-title">SUBSCRIBE TODAY AND SAVE 84%</p>, <p class="entry-subtitle">PAID SUBSCRIBERS GET A FREE SUBSCRIPTION TO THE AUTOMOBILE MAG APPLE EDITION!</p>, <p><span class="dropcap">T</span>he current <strong><a href="https://www.automobilemag.com/news/carbon-series-package-takes-39-pounds-2019-ford-gt/" target="_blank">Ford GT</a></strong> is a fine machine and a serious supercar, but if it\u2019s the original 2005-\u201906 GT that really gets your check-writing hand itchy, you may consider coming out to Barrett-Jackson\u2019s Scottsdale auction later this month. Over the course of a week, Barrett-Jackson will offer a total of eight first-generation Ford GTs for sale (of just over 4,000 ever built) and that kind of volume coupled with no-reserve bidding means that it\u2019s likely at least a couple of the GTs on offer will end up being a minor bargain for the buyer.</p>, <p><img alt="" class="size-content-width wp-image-1314941 aligncenter" data-base="https://st.automobilemag.com/uploads/sites/11/2019/01/2005-ford-gtx-1-roadster-side-view.jpg?interpolation=lanczos-none&amp;fit=around%7C660:371" data-lazy="1" height="371" src="https://st.automobilemag.com/wp-content/mu-plugins/ten-shared/assets/images/_.gif" width="660"/><noscript><img alt="" class="size-content-width wp-image-1314941 aligncenter" height="371" src="https://st.automobilemag.com/uploads/sites/11/2019/01/2005-ford-gtx-1-roadster-side-view.jpg?interpolation=lanczos-none&amp;fit=around%7C660:371" width="660"/></noscript></p>, <p>Our pick of the bunch is a 2005 Ford GTX-1 Roadster. The GTX-1 was an aftermarket roofless conversion of the original GT, inspired by the GT40 roadster prototype of the 1960s. Built by a third party, but supervised by Ford, just 100 GTX-1 Roadsters were produced and the first one built was shown at the 2005 <strong><a href="https://www.automobilemag.com/news/euro-gems-2018-sema-show/" target="_blank">SEMA show</a></strong>. Sure, the GTX-1 may lose a little torsional rigidity compared to the coupe, but given that most GTs are just used for street cruises anyway, we\u2019d guess the wind-in-the-hair experience (and added intensity of all that 5.4-liter V-8 noise) makes the conversion worthwhile.</p>, <p><img alt="" class="size-content-width wp-image-1314942 aligncenter" data-base="https://st.automobilemag.com/uploads/sites/11/2019/01/2006-ford-gt-heritage-edition-front-three-quarter.jpg?interpolation=lanczos-none&amp;fit=around%7C660:371" data-lazy="1" height="371" src="https://st.automobilemag.com/wp-content/mu-plugins/ten-shared/assets/images/_.gif" width="660"/><noscript><img alt="" class="size-content-width wp-image-1314942 aligncenter" height="371" src="https://st.automobilemag.com/uploads/sites/11/2019/01/2006-ford-gt-heritage-edition-front-three-quarter.jpg?interpolation=lanczos-none&amp;fit=around%7C660:371" width="660"/></noscript></p>, <p>If you prefer closed Ford GTs, there are plenty to choose from. If you\u2019re a fan of the <strong><a href="https://www.automobilemag.com/news/2019-ford-gt-heritage-edition-wears-gulf-livery-monterey/" target="_blank">Heritage Edition</a></strong> cars, done up in the blue and orange \u201cGulf\u201d-inspired livery, no fewer than three will cross the block in Scottsdale. Given that we like driving our cars, we\u2019ll take the highest mileage one, showing 3,092 miles on the odometer. The 335<sup>th</sup> built of just 343 Heritage Editions ever produced by Ford, this Canadian delivery car retains its original window stickers (one in English and one in French) and has had the airbag recalls performed already. Want a lower mileage Heritage Edition to just look at? The two other offerings have 75 miles and 288 miles on their odometers, respectively.</p>, <p><img alt="" class="size-content-width wp-image-1314943 aligncenter" data-base="https://st.automobilemag.com/uploads/sites/11/2019/01/2006-ford-gt-red-white-front-three-quarter-view.jpg?interpolation=lanczos-none&amp;fit=around%7C660:371" data-lazy="1" height="371" src="https://st.automobilemag.com/wp-content/mu-plugins/ten-shared/assets/images/_.gif" width="660"/><noscript><img alt="" class="size-content-width wp-image-1314943 aligncenter" height="371" src="https://st.automobilemag.com/uploads/sites/11/2019/01/2006-ford-gt-red-white-front-three-quarter-view.jpg?interpolation=lanczos-none&amp;fit=around%7C660:371" width="660"/></noscript></p>, <p>If you\u2019re a fan of the red with white stripe paint scheme on a closed GT, Barrett-Jackson will offer two of those: a 2005 with 52 miles to keep in your hermetically sealed garage and a 2006 with 2,746 miles that you could actually drive down to your local 7-11 every now and then.</p>, <p><img alt="" class="size-content-width wp-image-1314939 aligncenter" data-base="https://st.automobilemag.com/uploads/sites/11/2019/01/2005-ford-gt-modified-front-three-quarter.jpg?interpolation=lanczos-none&amp;fit=around%7C660:371" data-lazy="1" height="371" src="https://st.automobilemag.com/wp-content/mu-plugins/ten-shared/assets/images/_.gif" width="660"/><noscript><img alt="" class="size-content-width wp-image-1314939 aligncenter" height="371" src="https://st.automobilemag.com/uploads/sites/11/2019/01/2005-ford-gt-modified-front-three-quarter.jpg?interpolation=lanczos-none&amp;fit=around%7C660:371" width="660"/></noscript></p>, <p>That leaves just two modified Ford GTs: a 2006 in Tungsten Gray without stripes and 607 miles on the clock and an upgraded supercharger, or a 2005 in white with blue stripes, side scoops, and wheels that has been bumped up to 850 horsepower. [<p class="videoTitle">Study Up On Nutrition Before Going Vegan or Vegetarian</p>, <p class="boxLabel"> Link to this video </p>, <p class="boxLabel"> Embed this video </p>, <p class="replayButton"><a href="#" onclick="return false;">Replay</a></p>, <p class="related"> More videos (1 of 9)</p>, <p class="paragraph" data-pnum="1">Are you thinking about giving up meat?</p>, <p class="paragraph" data-pnum="2">Some people feel strongly about not eating animals and it can have a positive impact on the environment, but as Consumer Reports warns, when some people cut out meat and dairy, they need to take extra care to get the nutrients they need.</p>, <p class="paragraph" data-pnum="3">Consumer Reports suggests for a balanced vegetarian or vegan diet, you need to pay special attention to getting enough of these four important nutrients:  protein, calcium, iron and vitamin B12.</p>, <p class="paragraph" data-pnum="4">There are plenty of plant foods that have protein. For example - tofu, chickpeas, and other legumes, and high protein grains such as quinoa. Eat some protein at every meal.</p>, <p class="paragraph" data-pnum="5">And don't forget bone-building calcium. Doctors recommend 1,000 mg a day, and 1,200 if you\u2019re a woman over 50. How do you get it when don\u2019t eat dairy?</p>, <p class="paragraph" data-pnum="6">Plant sources of calcium include almonds, bok choy, collard greens, kale, fortified plant milk or orange juice and calcium-set tofu.</p>, <p class="paragraph" data-pnum="7">Getting enough iron can be a challenge when you don\u2019t eat meat. Pair good plant iron sources, such as lentils, white beans and other legumes, and swiss chard with vitamin C containing foods such as oranges and red bell peppers. Combining plant foods rich in iron with Vitamin C helps boost iron absorption.</p>, <p class="paragraph" data-pnum="8">Another nutrient you may miss out on: Vitamin B12, crucial for brain and nervous system functioning. Fortified plant milks, meat alternatives, breakfast cereals can help you get B12.</p>, <p class="paragraph" data-pnum="9">If you\u2019re planning on making the switch to veggie or vegan in the new year, it\u2019s not a bad idea to check in with your health care provider to ensure you\u2019re getting enough of the nutrients you need!</p>, <p class="paragraph" data-pnum="10">All Consumer Reports Material Copyright \xa9 2019_ Consumer Reports, Inc.</p>, <p class="paragraph" data-pnum="11">ALL RIGHTS RESERVED</p>, <p>\xa0\xa0</p>]
