[<p class="menu-toggle"></p>, <p><img alt="" class="attachment-featuredfull size-featuredfull wp-post-image" height="430" src="https://mk0nextbigfuturj5ioe.kinstacdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/bfrrefuel-730x430.png" title="" width="730"/></p>, <p>Many space plans propose different space vehicles for different roles and activities. There is a launcher that goes from Earth to low earth orbit or the launcher goes directly to higher orbits with lower mass. The SpaceX Super Heavy Starship should be flying to orbit by 2020 with a fully reusable rocket. It will be 2-4 more years before it is fully developed for commercial flights.</p>, <p>If it is flying with minimal maintenance for 100 trips then it will bring the cost of each space launch down to about $5 million per launch.</p>, <p>It appears to make sense for 5-10 years after the development of the commercial SpaceX Super Heavy Starship that various slightly modified versions are used in the role of orbital space tugs, fuel stations and orbit to moon and orbit to Mars vehicles.</p>, <p>It is similar to the old ideas about using the Space Shuttle fuel tanks back in the 1980s for space stations.</p>, <p>The SpaceX Super Heavy Starship can land back on Earth and would be able to act as a giant lander for the moon as well.</p>, <p>The Space Super Heavy Starship can bring mining equipment to the moon and make lunar fuel. Having vehicles and vehicles acting as refueling stations will greatly reduce the cost of moving around from space and not just to low earth orbit.</p>, <p>Going from low earth orbit to the surface of the moon takes about half of the fuel going from Earth to low earth orbit.</p>, <p>There could be SpaceX Super Heavy Starships placed into Lunar Cycling and Mars Cycling orbits.</p>, <p><img alt="" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-153112" height="838" src="https://mk0nextbigfuturj5ioe.kinstacdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/fuelspacex.jpg" width="1440"/></p>, <p>Simplifying to have modifications of one vehicle for all of the roles in Space would reduce the development costs. [<p>Google\u2019s \u201cSmall Business Community\u201d message board is shutting down, according to an announcement published on January 2nd.</p>, <p>The Small Business Community is officially shutting down on January 16th.</p>, <p>The <a href="https://www.gsmallbusiness.com/forum/view_topic/67/1500/Reach-Your-Customers/Bad-Review-from-your-competitors" rel=" noopener" target="_blank">announcement</a> states:</p>, <p>\u201cThank you for being a member of the Small Business Community from Google. We will keep you posted on any future Community efforts. We hope you\u2019ve made many connections as a member, and will continue to benefit from those relationships in the future.\u201d</p>, <p>The Small Business Community from Google was a space where business owners could access resources, share information with each other, and organize meet-ups.</p>, <p>If you\u2019re not familiar with it, that\u2019s likely because it was only open to small business owners in a handful of pilot cities in the US.</p>, <p>It\u2019s possible Google may have opened the community up to users in more cities, however, the project never made it out of beta.</p>, <p>The community does not appear to be very active. [<p>Back in April, I quit as a longtime AT&amp;T wireless customer and <a href="https://www.houstonchronicle.com/techburger/article/I-switched-from-AT-T-to-T-Mobile-Here-s-why-and-12878340.php">made the leap to using T-Mobile for my family\u2019s cellular provider</a>. I was lured by a much smaller price tag, much faster data speeds and a much-improved service footprint for the nation\u2019s third-largest carrier.</p>, <p>Eight months later, it\u2019s time for an update. In fact, I\u2019ve had quite a few emailed and social-media requests for a report on how it\u2019s working out. So, here\u2019s a scorecard:</p>, <p><strong>PRICING</strong>: <strong>A</strong></p>, <p>My main reason for ending a 20-year relationship with AT&amp;T was price. I was paying $175 a month for two phone lines; data access for two Apple Watches; and an allowance of 16 gigabytes of data. T-Mobile offers those 55 and older a great deal: two lines with unlimited data, text and voice for $70 a month. The Apple Watches added $10 each to make the final price $90, saving us $85 a month over AT&amp;T.</p>, <p><strong>NOT-SO-HAPPY CAMPER:\xa0<a href="https://www.houstonchronicle.com/techburger/article/Switching-to-T-Mobile-with-a-side-of-Apple-13174768.php">Switching to <span class="gsa-hit-highlight">T</span>-<span class="gsa-hit-highlight">Mobile</span>, with a side of Apple: Confusion, exhaustion, frustration</a></strong></p>, <p><a href="https://www.houstonchronicle.com/techburger/article/Switching-to-T-Mobile-with-a-side-of-Apple-13174768.php"></a>Near the end of December, T-Mobile was offering a promotion that allowed us to add our daughter to our 55+ plan for just $20 a month, bringing our total payment to $110 a month. She had been on an AT&amp;T prepay plan for $25 a month, but with no data. I was told by a T-Mobile rep via chat that this is not a promotional price that will go up. We\u2019ll see. (The extra-line promotion, by the way, is no longer available.)</p>, <p>Also, note that these prices include a discount if you use AutoPay. If you choose not to use it, each line costs an additional $5. Without AutoPay, we\u2019d pay another $25 monthly.</p>, <p><strong>DATA SPEED: A-</strong></p>, <p>T-Mobile consistently outperforms the speeds I was seeing with AT&amp;T in the places where I live, work and play. On speed tests taken periodically at my various stomping grounds, I\u2019ll get anywhere between 40-95 Mbps downloads when I\u2019ve got a full four bars. There are some exceptions, however.</p>, <p><strong>ZOOM:\xa0<a href="https://www.houstonchronicle.com/techburger/article/How-fast-is-cellular-data-service-in-Texas-13086818.php">How fast is cellular data service in Texas cities?</a></strong></p>, <p>I frequently travel between Houston and my parents\u2019 home in Corpus Christi, and there are several spots along that route where T-Mobile\u2019s service drops to a weak one bar, or I get the dreaded \u201cNo Service\u201d notification. Fortunately, the dropouts don\u2019t last long. Occasional dropouts were also an issue on a trip <a href="https://www.houstonchronicle.com/techburger/article/Road-trip-Taking-our-new-T-Mobile-service-to-San-12894061.php">earlier this year to San Antonio</a>.</p>, <p>I\u2019m particularly happy with upload speeds, which handily beat the paltry 5 Mbps uploads I get with my Comcast broadband connection. Upload speeds are often near or just below download speeds. Often, if I need to upload something large, I\u2019ll use my iPhone rather than a computer connected to Comcast at home to get the job done.</p>, <p>As with other carriers, T-Mobile may slow your speeds on its \u201cunlimited\u201d accounts after you reach a certain threshold \u2014 but that limit is much higher. On AT&amp;T, Verizon and Sprint, you may be slowed once you pass 22 gigabytes of data. On T-Mobile, the threshold is 50 GB. So far, we\u2019ve come nowhere near that point.</p>, <p>Unfortunately, I\u2019m not as happy with one particular aspect of T-Mobile\u2019s speeds.</p>, <p><strong>MOBILE HOTSPOT: C-</strong></p>, <p>The carrier\u2019s standard T-Mobile One account gives you a mobile hotspot, allowing you to connect other devices via Wi-Fi to share data. But unlike AT&amp;T\u2019s mobile hotspot feature that connects at full LTE speeds, T-Mobile throttles its users back to 3G speeds.</p>, <p>If all you are doing is checking email, sending messages or using another text-based application, this slowness is merely annoying. But if you are looking at websites, sending or receiving photos or video, or trying to stream music, T-Mobile\u2019s hotspot is almost useless, particularly if you have two or fewer bars.</p>, <p><strong>SPEED TEST:\xa0<a href="https://www.houstonchronicle.com/techburger/article/PC-Magazine-testing-ranks-cellular-speeds-across-12985660.php">PCMag testing ranks cellular speeds across Houston</a></strong></p>, <p>There is a way to get full LTE speeds on a hotspot, however, by paying more. T-Mobile lets you upgrade to its One Plus service for an additional $15 a month, with a limit of 20GB of LTE hotspot data. One Plus gets you other benefits, including full HD streaming and faster data speeds when traveling to any of 210 countries. I wish T-Mobile would break out the hotspot boost \u2014 I\u2019d pay another $5 a month to get faster hotspot speeds.</p>, <p><strong>VOICE CALLS: B+</strong></p>, <p>For the most part, voice calls are of good quality, particularly when using Wi-Fi calling, or the enhanced LTE feature known as HD Voice. When those aren\u2019t present, though, T-Mobile\u2019s voice calls sometimes don\u2019t match up to what I experienced with AT&amp;T, but those times are rare.</p>, <p>I do get the occasional dropped call with T-Mobile, but then again, I did with AT&amp;T, too. And you can never be sure whether the issue is on your end or on that of the person you\u2019re talking to.</p>, <p><strong>CUSTOMER SERVICE: A-</strong></p>, <p>I have only had to use T-Mobile\u2019s customer service a few times, but so far it has been very good. Representatives contacted via chat and phone have been knowledgeable and efficient. Any issues I had were addressed quickly and to my satisfaction.</p>, <p>I did, however, have one unpleasant surprise early on. An additional charge for an unwanted international calling plan showed up on my account. I was able to get it removed, but not before it was billed, and then a refund was issued. It didn\u2019t cost me anything in the end other than aggravation.</p>, <p><strong>COMING SOON:\xa0<a href="https://www.houstonchronicle.com/business/article/5G-promises-Houstonians-faster-internet-more-12925741.php">5G promises Houstonians faster internet, more choice</a></strong></p>, <p>One other small gripe: T-Mobile\u2019s website and app don\u2019t always allow the same kind of self-service capabilities as AT&amp;T. For example, when I wanted to add my daughter with the $20-a-month service, I had either to call or go to a T-Mobile store \u2014 it couldn\u2019t be added online.</p>, <p><strong>EXTRAS AND PERKS: B</strong></p>, <p>T-Mobile offers a lot of extra incentives, but not all of them are available with the Unlimited 55+ account. For example, regular T-Mobile One customers get a free Netflix account, but that\u2019s not available for 55+ users.</p>, <p>The carrier also has an app called T-Mobile Tuesdays, which has a new set of freebies every week. Many of these don\u2019t interest me \u2014 discounted concert tickets, for example \u2014 while others are intriguing. But, they\u2019re not enough to keep me opening the app every Tuesday to see what\u2019s new. Others, though, may find them worthwhile.</p>, <p><strong>OVERALL GRADE: B+</strong></p>, <p>The final grade is dragged down by T-Mobile\u2019s hotspot issues, but if that\u2019s not a big deal for you, then consider the general score to be an A-. We\u2019re very happy we\u2019ve made the switch, and look forward to seeing how T-Mobile handles the upcoming transition to 5G.</p>, <p>(Read my original story about switching at <a href="https://houstonchronicle.com/tmobileswitch" target="_blank">houstonchronicle.com/tmobileswitch</a>, and a followup at <a href="https://www.houstonchronicle.com/techburger/article/Road-trip-Taking-our-new-T-Mobile-service-to-San-12894061.php" target="_blank">houstonchronicle.com/tmobilesa</a>.)</p>, <p><em> </em></p>, <p><em>dwight.silverman@chron.com</em></p>, <p><em> </em></p>, <p><em>twitter.com/dsilverman</em></p>, <p><em>\n<p>houstonchronicle.com/techburger</p>\n</em></p>, <p>houstonchronicle.com/techburger</p>, <p>Dwight Silverman is the technology editor for the Houston Chronicle. He manages the TechBurger website, and writes about personal technology for HoustonChronicle.com, Chron.com and the print edition.</p>, <p>He previously was the senior web producer for premium products, managing HoustonChronicle.com, the Chronicle's iPad app and E-edition.</p>, <p>He also has worked as the social media manager and technology blogger for the Houston Chronicle and Chron.com. He has been with the Houston Chronicle since 1990, and has worked as an assistant state editor, business reporter, technology columnist and interactive journalism editor. He moved to the website staff in 2000 and was responsible for helping bring blogging and social media to chron.com.</p>, <p>He's also worked at the San Antonio Current, the San Antonio Light and the Beaumont Enterprise.</p>, <p>Silverman is a former co-host of Technology Bytes, a weekly computer call-in show on KPFT-FM. It\u2019s time for him to leave his old Honda Accord behind and get a nice island car to enjoy the sand and the sun. What should he buy?<br/></p>, <p><em>(Welcome back to <a href="http://jalopnik.com/tag/wcsyb" onclick="window.ga('send', 'event', 'Embedded Url', 'Internal link', 'http://jalopnik.com/tag/wcsyb', {metric25:1})" rel="nofollow">What Car Should You Buy</a>?
